<Author>Traveler from CA
<Content>Reasonable place to stay in SF We stayed overnight at the Castle Inn in San Francisco in November. It was a fairly convenient to Alcatraz Island and California Academy of Science in Golden Gate Park. We were looking for a reasonably priced  convenient location in SF that we did not have to pay for parking.  Very basic motel with comfortable beds, mini refrig and basic continental breakfast. It was within walking distance to quite a few restaurants (Miller's East Coast Deli-yummy!)  I did find that the clerk at the desk was rather unfriendly, though helpful. The free parking spaces were extremely tight for our mini van. The noise was not too bad, being only 1 block from Van Ness Ave.  If you are looking for a no frills, comfortable place to stay, Castle Inn was a good choice.

<Author>DamLou
<Content>Ideal and very very friendly. Just about everything you read on tripadvisor about the Castle Inn is true. It is15mins walk down to F/Wharf or 15mins up to Union Square / Chinatown area. Simple but sufficient complimentary breakfast (coffee, good orange juice, yoghurt, fruit, pastry, cereal bars) left us satisfied (including 2 teenagers!). Stayed in the 2 bedroom-suite. A little noise from the street, and some noise from the ice machine just outside the room, but with ear plugs in (always travel with them!), had a good night's sleep. San Francisco is an expensive city, and the Castle Inn offers excellent value. Special mention to Varsa, the effusively helpful manageress, who provided all sorts of details about tours and transport. We could not have enjoyed SF as much without her help. There is an excellent Thai restaurant - simple, fast service and great value - just 3 doors away for a convenient meal. In advance of us arriving, we had asked Varsa to book us onto a city tour with Tower Tours including the Alcatraz tour, and I would fully recommend this, because you will get to see the slightly more out-of-town sights like twin peaks, Golden Gate Park, leaving you to explore the inner city stuff on foot later. Don't miss out Alcatraz - it is incredible. Our family really enjoyed US Pampanito too. Different!If I was a millionaire I'd stay in a luxury hotel. But as a family, out sightseeing from early after breakfast until after our evening meal, the Castle Inn is absolutely ideal.

<Content>Great location, tired rooms. Stayed for 4 nights in the 2 bedroom suite as the first stop on a trip down the east coast. Briliant location, busses run on the two streets either side(Van Ness  Polk), so transport links were great for any location. Back to the hotel, reception was small but the staff were helpfull, the suite faced onto the street and did suffer noise, but heck you are in a city it never troubled us. <Author>Devonmen
<Content>Good Clean Affordable Accomodation We stayed here in May 2008 based on the reviews on here! We weren't dissapointed. Just to be clear upfront - this is not a luxury hotel by any means, but for the price and location you couldn't ask for much more. The rooms were clean and had fridge and microwave which was a bonus. The shower was hot and the pressure good. What really set this apart though was the customer service we received from Varsa at the front desk. She couldn't have been more helpful, whipping out a map of the city of San Fran as soon as we checked in, circling all the best places to go, and highlighting the areas to avoid. We parked the car in their free car park (which we didn't find too tight or small contrary to other reviews on here, though we could understand how some may have found it a little tight in places). The car wasn't needed for our stay though as the hotel is just a few yards from a main bus route so we got a 3 day MUNI pass and used the frequent buses and trams during our stay. Breakfast is literally some baskets of pre-packaged Danishes Pastries and Nutrigrain bars, with Coffee and Orange Juice available. Nothing glamorous but adequate if you just want to grab a bite on your way out! There are also many eateries within a stones throw of the hotel (we recommend 'Polkers').The hotel is not going to be for everyone, particularly those who want or need to maybe spend a lot of time in their hotel room, but if you are looking for affordable, clean and safe accomodation in San Francisco, then this would be a good choice to make.

<Author>djalk
<Content>Good low cost place to stay Four ladies wanting a low cost and safe place to stay while in San Francisco. The Castle Inn was a great choice for us. Loved the free off street parking (fit the full size car just fine) and location. The free continental breakfast (yougert, granola bars, fruit, pasteries) were great to bring back to our room or take and go. Nothing fancy but good and basic. The free hot chocolate at night was appreciated as it gets cold outside at night. We walked -downhill- to Fisherman's Warf and spent the day there and a $10 taxi ride brought us back in the evening. The next day we spent the $11 each and bought an all day pass for the cable car/bus transportation. The pass got us all over town. The cable car stop is 2 blocks away and the bus stop is a block away. The local resturants were reasonably priced and pleasant. The room had a refrigerator and microwave (to heat up leftover resturant food). Liked how the sink was outside of the bathroom, making it easier for the four of us to get ready in the morning. The rooms were clean and quiet (we were on the 3rd floor). The hotel personnel were friendly and helpful. If you are looking to be pampered the pay the extra to stay elsewhere but if you want a clean, basic hotel then stay here. There is too much to see and do in San Francisco to spend time in the hotel room anyway.

<Author>Wolin
<Content>Recommend The Castle Inn We highly recommend The Castle Inn if you are looking for a good, clean, quiet value for money budget motel located on Russian Hill. It is a walk, cable car or bus ride to Fisherman鈥檚 Wharf (eat at Scomas, everywhere else seems to be tourist traps) and everywhere else. It is close to public transport with connections that can take you all over SF. We walked a few blocks and then rode buses to Coit Tower, Haight Ashbury, AMC Cinema and the Golden Gate Bridge for instance.Varsa was very helpful with our Internet booking and Marshall was super friendly and helpful on check-in. He looked after our luggage for us when we arrived early the morning of check-in. Marshall gave us a map and wrote down the places to see (and the areas to avoid). Varsa arranged some very good tours for us.The hotel is close to many many restaurants that offer delicious and fresh food at reasonable prices, mostly on Polk Street. We stayed a week and ate very well each night in a different establishment. Also on Polk is a Walgreens drug store (pharmacy/supermarket) and organic markets. Polk hosts a very good value laundry and dry cleaner (turn right from the Castle Inn, cross Polk and turn right, you will find it just up the hill from Broadway).The rooms are a good size and clean; we had a non-smoking room with a comfortable queen bed. There is some street noise, but not intrusive. We heard footsteps from the room above.The breakfast is not that good tho: lots of fat, sugar and carbs. We purchased fruit, yogurt and granola from the organic market on Polk (the market has plastic spoons available free of charge, we ate the granola from the cups in the room). The 鈥榝ridge and microwave were very useful.Marshall can arrange a Town Car transfer. The fare from the airport was $55. You can call the car direct on 415 756 7402, ask for Jun.We will return to San Francisco and stay at the Castle Inn.

<Author>Madrid_Traveller
<Content>Great location We spent 7 days at the Castle Inn at the beginning of this month. Booking the hotel was really easy and Varsa came back confirming the booking and rest of details. Getting to the hotel from the airport is very simple as it is close to Van Ness ( 101). In less than 30 minutes you are there. The location of the hotel is excellent for traveling around ( 49 miles scenic route, Napa, Marine County,..) and also for using public transportation as the cable car taking you to the center or to Fisherman's Wharf is at two blocks distance. There are also a couple of buses at Van Ness which takes you downtown.Although some people at this site complain about noise, the only noise that sometimes was disturbing was the neighbors' one. The walls seem to be really thin and anything happening next door is like if was happening inside the room. We were at one of the middle rooms of the third floor and from there we hardly listen any noise from the nearby avenue. Room was OK and better than what you can expect from the price you pay. It is modest but very clean and with no carpet smell ( something that sometimes you cannot avoid at US or UK hotels where there are carpets everywhere). We did not use the microwave or the fridge as we spent most of the time out either traveling in the area or just enjoying the city. I understand that these facilities may be better appreciated by families traveling with children.Last, I would like to highlight the great information provided by Varsa on arrival, letting us know about highlights, things we should not miss and other tips. The same in the mornings, making sure that everyone can get what they want for breakfast. She really cares and makes you feel like at home. By the way, the same cannot be say about the other person who was there when Varsa was off. I recommend the Castle Inn for group of friends, families and everyone who wants to explore the city and enjoy holidays.

<Author>pbeary
<Content>great location, service and price overall rating reflects heavy emphasis on value - this is far from a luxury, or a new or a newly refurbished or a full service hotel.the high value experience begins with booking and communicating directly with Varsa. her email communication is excellent - even when away from the inn on holiday. she booked a tour for us, responded with advice on itinerary scheduling, restaurant recommendations (pesce and yabbies coastal kitchen were both excellent), and advice on public transportation and possible walks. they secured our luggage for us when we arrived early the morning of check-in and let us park through the dinner hour after check-out. value for the price: $99 + 14% tax @ night for a double queen in an interesting  fun area of san francisco (in march) with FREE PARKING. our room offered a decent tv, desk/chair, small area with counter/mirror, hanging, frig  microwave adjacent to room with toilet/shower. the furnishings and conditions were clean and adequate (not new or strikingly attractive). the beds were comfortable and fairly firm with some give. Our room was in the middle of the 2nd floor of a three floor structure. it is not thoroughly insulated. we heard some noise above of us one night and some street noise (it's a half block off of Van Ness). the noise fits in with the feel of a busy neighborhood - which we enjoyed. there are many restaurant choices for varying budgets within easy walking distance. we also walked to fisherman's wharf. We took the trolley or the bus to most sights. we did drive to muir woods (we thoroughly enjoyed our walk through there) and to one dinner on the coast at Sutro's at the Cliff House (absolutely incredible). We obviously enjoyed our stay at the castle inn.

<Author>JNS_714
<Content>The Good, The Bad and the So So Location - The Good - location for using the local transit - short walks to the Muni bus and cable car line. The Bad - location is Noisy! - lots of traffic noise from Van Ness and Broadway. We had a 2nd floor room mid-way in the building. Bring ear-plugs if truck horns, sirens, traffic, Harley-Davidsons roaring by keep you from sleeping. The walls are thin and you can hear every conversation in the adjacent rooms, as well as the plumbing.Staff - Friendly staff ready to help people from out of town - especially for knowing where NOT to go after dark or if you are traveling with kids.Facilities - rooms were clean. Nice having the microwave and compact refrigerator. Beds were satisfactory. Bring your laptop and take advantage of the WiFi to check the SF MTA routes and schedules. Take heed about the parking area - not designed for full sized SUVs.Don't forget the 13% city hotel tax when budgeting your trip!

<Author>cubbyboy1991
<Content>Great motel, but... The Castle Inn is a great find if you're looking for a great motel. It's not a hotel. It's a good, inexpensive stay in an expensive city. Just about everything you've read is true. Marshall at the front desk was extremely nice and helpful. The location, other than being on a listless patch of concrete called Broadway Ave, is terrific, centrally located to all of SF and around the block from a Strabucks, a Peets, a great bagel place and a Real Foods market, in addition to a wonderfully charming neighborhood. Free parking, free internet, all very good. But here's the one warning:The family suite, where I stayed with my wife and our two kids, had room to spare, but it's noisy. The ice machine is right outside the door and it recycles regularly, and the front of the room is over the street and very noisy. Cars, trucks, etc, especially during the morning rush. You've been warned.

<Author>cankid
<Content>Castle Inn, San Francisco The Castle Inn is a Motel with external hallways/room entrances located in the Polk Street area of San Francisco. The rooms are best described as spartan with amenities including parking, wireless internet, continental breakfast, microwave and two-door fridge. The noise levels from street level traffic, as well as motel guest traffic, are high and disconcerting at times. The continental breakfast is misleading and not accurately reflected on the website (nor by comments from the owners).Our expectations, derived primarily from TripAdvisor's ranking of the Castle Inn (at the time 11th among approx. 230 San Francisco Hotels), were not met. Although all amenities listed on the Castle Inn's website were offered, the motel should not be included/compared with Hotels (this may be a TripAdvisor concern/problem). Unfortunately for travelers (anticipating a Hotel) and the Castle Inn, the opportunity for disappointment arises directly from these ratings.We found much better accommodation and value in San Francisco.

<Author>FaceLid
<Content>A Gem in the Heart of San Fran! We (2 couples) stayed at the Castle Inn for two nights (Jan 2-4 2008) and couldn鈥檛 have been more pleased with our experience. Our room rate with tax was about $90 per night. Upon our check-in, we were warmly greeted by Varsa, who not only assisted us with our check-in, but also provided directions/maps, recommendations to numerous restaurants, as well as printed out our boarding passes for the next leg of our trip. One of our rooms was in the front and faced Broadway, the other more towards the back. Both rooms were clean, roomy, comfy, and quiet. Noise was not an issue for either room. Both rooms also included a coffee maker w/coffee, refrigerator, and microwave. We brewed our coffee each morning, and used the 鈥榝ridge鈥?and 鈥榳ave鈥?to keep and reheat our leftovers. We started our mornings early, so grabbing breakfast to go from the office-- fruit, muffins, breakfast bars, yogurt, juice鈥o name a few, was a bonus. Parking was not an issue either. It may be a little tight, but totally manageable.All in all, the Castle Inn is a great place, whether you call it an inn, motel, hotel, or whatever you want to name it. The price was in line with the amenities that were offered, and I will, without a doubt, stay here again on my next visit.And here鈥檚 a note to the complainers: WAKE UP! This is San Francisco 鈥?the fact that they have parking, and it is free, is a bonus; the fact that they offer 鈥済rab-n-go鈥?breakfast, is a bonus; and the fact that they are conveniently located in a safe neighborhood near shopping and restaurants, is a bonus! If you would have done your homework before checking in, you would have known what to expect.

<Author>tkeefe
<Content>Great Location for Staying in the City, Ok for the Price The Castle Inn is an older motel type establishment. Slightly run down and sparten but clean and very well managed by a friendly and helpful couple. Our room was clean and the only issue I had was that the walls and floors did little to keep out noise from other rooms (were those elephants above us?). Stay in an upper floor I would guess to lessen this problem. Here's the bonuses: FREE PARKING! Also, you are situated right on the edge of a fun neighborhood on Polk Street. Lots of good restaurants, bars and local shops in easy walking distance. Also if you want to get around town, a cable car is 3 blocks away (best way to get downtown!) and a bunch of city buses (MUNI) stop nearby to take you almost anywher in the city pretty quick. I'll be staying here again.

<Author>ljr88888
<Content>Not as good as I expected I guess I had high expectations after reading all the glowing reviews on Trip Advisor. We stayed at the Castle Inn for 5 nights over Christmas. Location is pretty good ... only 3 blocks from the cable car line and about 10 blocks to the waterfront. Buses run up and down Van Ness St. The staff kept the room very clean. But the walls of this place were paper-thin! The first night there were two couples in the next room talking and laughing loudly until 2 a.m. ... then they started up again at 7 a.m. If they hadn't checked out I would have asked to be moved because it was impossible to sleep. The next neighbors must have packed all their clothes in plastic sacks because they were constantly rattling sacks ... yes, we could hear this through the walls. The continental breakfast consisted of coffee, some store-bought gooey pastries and fruit. Fortunately there was a great diner across the street - Peter D's - where you can get a real breakfast. Yes, parking is free but negotiating the tiny cramped garage is quite a challenge. We got the room for only $99-$115 during our stay but I was looking longingly at the Holiday Inn down the street wondering if it was any better.

<Author>Giltedge
<Content>Good Choice for the Price We stayed at the Castle Inn for two nights. We flew into SFO and took the Bart to the Civic Center station and then rode the Muni bus #47 to the Broadway stop. This put us within a half block from the motel. Our room was very pleasant. It had a two door refrigerator, microwave, comfortable queen size bed, and was very clean. It is an older motel but appears very well taken care of. Our continental breakfast included danish, fruit, yogurt and juice. Since we enjoy walking, we took in Fisherman's Wharf, Alcartraz, Giradehelli Square and China Town on foot. Be prepared to walk up and down hills to get to any of these locations. The trolley and buses though are a good alternative to walking if you get tired of trudging up and down the hills of San Francisco. I would stay at this motel again and would recommend it to others as a very good place to stay at a very reasonable price.

<Author>mindaway
<Content>Perfect base Booked this Inn after checking the reviews on tripadvisor and was not let down. The Inn makes a perfect base to visit the city. As first timers to SF, 3 of us stayed at the Inn for 4 nights during the month of October and we were highly satisfied. The room with 2 double beds was roomy enough to fit all our luggage and still make us feel comfortable (we were traveling from overseas and doing a 3-week trip through California). It was clean, quiet (guess low season helped too) and the people at the front desk were extremely helpful (numerous maps and advices were given and they helped us booked our car service to the airport, etc.). The Inn is 5 minutes from one of the main trolley lines, next door to some bus lines and a 20-30 minute walk to Grant Ave. in Chinatown. Bus passes can be bought 5 minutes away as well. The coffee maker in the room as well as additional coffee, hot chocolate, OJ, muffins, fruits, etc. available at the front office early in the am makes it ideal to get ready early in the morning to go explore the city all day. The free parking was wonderful too.All in all, we had a very pleasant stay, with amazing prices for such a nice location and for all the little extras we had. would definitely stay there again.

<Author>travelersIndiana
<Content>Great little Inn in San Francisco My husband and I stayed at the Castle Inn for our first trip to San Francisco. It was just what we were looking for. We didn't want to stay in the hustle and bustle of the Wharf and this was perfect. It was in a quiet neighborhood away from all the tourist areas. The room was not an upscale luxury room but clean and comfortable with a microwave and fridge/freezer, after all we were there to see the sights and not spend all our time in a motel. Within walking distance is a Subway, donut shop, Escape from New York pizza, Peter D's (open for breakfast and lunch and has a great breakfast), Walgreens, Starbucks, a Tai restaurant, a local bar/restaraunt (excellent hamburgers), and a small grocery. We felt safe walking to these places. We purchased a 7 day muni pass that gets you on any bus, cable car, bart, and f-market street car. The passes are 24.00 but well worth it. A one way trip on the cable car is 5.00 so the pass is the best way to go. Marshall, at the hotel desk, gave us a map of the bus routes and gave us information on where to go, how to get there and where not to go. We asked about some tours and Arlene called and made our reservations and we got a discount from the hotel booking for us. They were very helpful and we really appreaciated their information as this was our first trip.As for the breakfast, it was as advertised, a continental breakfast. It was perfect for someone in a hurry to get going in the morning. We took advantage of this our first morning but then went out for breakfast or purchased donuts around the corner to have in our room. We enjoyed our stay at the Castle Inn and would stay there again if we ever get to return to San Francisco.

<Author>Cutes12
<Content>Quiet, Clean, Great Value -Best Little Motel in SF! The Castle Inn is our favorite small hotel in San Francisco! We have stayed there on 2 occasions  the wonderful staff, convenient location,  clean, quiet rooms keep us coming back! Located at Broadway  Van Ness, Castle Inn is in a nice neighborhood with drug store, grocery, cafes  cute shops within close walking distance. It's also right on the bus line  is a straight shot down to Fisherman's Wharf. My dad  I stayed for 4 quiet  comfortable nights. We rented a car on our previous trip, but found that with a little planning, getting around on the bus was an easier  less costly option. The Castle Inn does offer free parking though, which is a real bonus in SF! Parking throughout SF is difficult, pricey  hard to find. For this trip, we purchased 3-day Muni Passes at the airport when we arrived,  used those to travel the city on busses  cable cars - a good value if you don't mind the challenges of riding city busses! Make sure you get a bus route map when you purchase your Muni Passes!Rooms at the Castle are clean  comfortable - not fancy or large, but decent  reasonably priced compared to many SF hotels. Our 2-bed room had a hairdryer, small fridge, coffee maker, free cable tv  table with 2 large chairs. Our 3rd floor room overlooked a lovely yard of trees next door  we could just see a bit of the Golden Gate Bridge in the distance. There is a nice little continental breakfast (coffee, cocoa, yogurt, fruit, pastries, granola bars) in the lobby. The best feature of the Castle Inn is our favorite hostess, Versa! She is always so pleasant, accomodating  knowledgeable with good advice about the city. They also gave us a chart showing busses/stop locations to go to various tourist locations throughout the city. Castle Inn also has a nice website worth checking out.If you want a clean, decent room to sleep in at night  a hot shower in the morning without a lot of pricey luxury, the Castle Inn is a little gem of a motel in a convenient location to get to the tourist attractions easily. I have  will continue to recommend San Francisco's Castle Inn to anyone considering a trip to the City by the Bay!  
<Date>Oct 12, 2007

<Content>It Gets My Best Rating Trip Advisor reader comments is what convinced my wife  I to stay at THE CASTLE INN. My wife  both enjoyed everything...here are the highlights for you;HOTEL; clean, great value, on site parking so you can access your car easily, modest but sufficient breakfast...enough to get you out  on your way, clean sheets/towels daily of good quality, cleaned the bathroom daily (cleaned it, not just wipe off the counter) hotel is small'ish which makes it easy to get around.WiFi worked perfectly, even at the last room on the end where we were.STAFF; you'll be hard pressed to find any staff at ANY hotel that will give you the attention and GENUINE service of these folks...period. Hosts(not front desk clerks) Marshall  Arlene are good folks that make you feel at home. (any city for that matter)NEIGHBORHOOD; Just like it sounds, it's a neighborhood, it's safe, actually friendly/socialble, great variety of eateries. In this neighborhood, you felt as if you were part of the local rythems. We actually strolled the neighborhood one afternoon just to enjoy it. We came in late every evening, walking most of the time, without any problems. LOCATION; centrally located (meaning easy to drive to  from going any direction) great walking access to wharf, china town, 2 blocks to cable car, Lombard St., etc.SINCE YOU'VE READ THIS FAR, here's a tip for you...if you enjoy fine food in a small, but casual/sophisticated atmosphere, visit a restaurant on the corner of Hyde  Green (4 blocks from TCI on the cable car line) named FRASCATI. We stumbled on to it walking back from the wharf one night...it was one of those little discoveries you make accidentally that you'll talk about everytime you remember your trip to San Francisco. Hope this has helped you...enjoy THE CASTLE INN and San Francisco...we loved it!!

<Author>RolnRokk
<Content>Good Room, Wonderful Staff, Amazing Value Stayed here for Labor Day weekend with my wife and 8 year old son. Arrived 2 hours before check-in and room was ready. The clean, basic hotel room had everything we needed. Beds were comfortable and sheets/towels were good quality. Noise from the outside was minimal. My only recomendation would be to update the bathroom. The fridge and microwave are great for snacks. The complementary breakfast with fruit, yogurt, muffins and juice saved us time and money. The central location is perfect - walking distance from many tourist destinations (Wharf, Chinatown), but the neighborhood away from the crowds made us feel like locals. Walgreens, Starbucks, market, and numerous restaurants from pizza to fine dining are within a few blocks.The staff was unbelievably friendly and helpful, giving us an overview of the area and the major attractions at check-in. We didn't have a car so the cheat sheet showing public transportation routes and transfers to 20+ areas and attractions was useful. Both restaurants they recommended (sushi and Italian) were excellent. The day before our departure, we gave them our flight information and while we were out they checked us into our flight and printed our boarding passes so we would get the A section for Southwest. They also let us check out 2+ hours late so we could get last minute sightseeing done without toting our bags around.For the bargain price the stay was extremely pleasant. We will definitely stay here again.

<Author>mudmama
<Content>Delightful 5 night stay Having found this hotel by reading other reviews on tripadvisor.com, we wanted to second the comments left by other travellers and add our own opinion.We stayed 5 nights at the Castle Inn. We are a family of three, two parents and one 12-year old child, staying in the area primarily for a trip in California that will take us to all the major league baseball stadiums. While in San Francisco we also wanted to see the major tourist attractions. The Castle Inn was the perfect locale for us.The Inn's location is superior, 1/2 block to a major bus line, 3 blocks to the busline that goes to AT  T park. We were able to walk to Fisherman's Wharf, Lombard Street and Chinatown. These walks are definitely for those in good physical condition. We were also able to go by bus to Golden Gate Park and Haight Ashbury. We chose to drive our rental car (parked FREE at the Castle Inn) to Muir Woods, Berkeley and Oakland (McAfee Stadium, for the A's game).Re: parking at the Castle Inn. Other reviewers have said that parking is tricky because the lot is small. Yes, but if you have a compact car or are a seasoned driver, you will have no difficulty. Do not let these comments deter you from staying here.Our room was very large (#229). Unable to secure a room with two beds, we booked a king room with a rollaway bed for our son. We had optimal room all around, plenty of room for our suitcases and belongings. We never felt cramped.Our room rate for our stay was $189/night + taxes. We felt this was a steal compared to the price of other hotels who would also charge for parking and wi-fi access (luxury hotels, when will they get a clue??). The room was very clean, sheets, towels and soap / cups refreshed daily.The breakfast included was nothing to speak of. Our son loved the cello-wrapped cinnamon rolls, but we prefered to pocket some cereal / granola bars for our day trips and get our breakfast from Peet's coffee and the Bagelry (just around the corner).Checkout is 11 a.m. You need to vacate your room prior to checkout -- apparently the owners had some difficulty with travellers using the telephone and incurring charges after checksing out.

<Author>arlenejoe
<Content>A practical San Francisco gem What value for the location - just off Polk Street, close to Chinatown and Northbeach, and around the corner from Van Ness. This is a practical little hotel with free parking for guests, a lovely guest room with a comfortable bed, plush towels, granite and tile bathroom, coffee and amenities. Yet, this is a modest two-star hotel that gives you the basics without skimping. It's noisy outside with the cars and hustle bustle that make SF the great city that it is, but close the windows and you don't hear a thing. The front desk staff was warm, friendly, down home, and unpretentious. Wonderful neighborhood restaurants abound within walking distance, and the rate was gentle on our pocketbook. We will definitely return, as it is a good base for our SF touring.

<Author>BP_Traveler_39
<Content>A solid choice with very good location We stayed here for two nights at the end of our weeklong road trip along the Pacific Coast Highway starting in LA. The location is excellent. Parking is free (beware of what other hotels charge for this). Once we arrived, we parked the rental and didn't move it again until we left. This hotel is right near bus routes 47 and 49 and not that far from the starting point of the California Cable Car Line (California and Van Ness). If you ride the cable cars and buses a few times each in a given day, buy the all-you-can-ride day pass. Varsa (owner) was very helpful on the phone when I made the reservation. She wasn't there when we stayed, (would have liked to chat with her in person), but the husband and wife team working helped us with restaurants, maps, where to avoid, where best to catch the cable cars, etc. The room is decent size for the city. It was fairly quiet, and very clean. The elevator worked well. It was nice having a fridge since we were leaving early for the airport on our 2nd day. I'd recommend stocking up on food from the Real Food organic market just around the corner on Polk St (kinda pricey, but aren't most organic markets). Breakfast at this hotel was skimpy but I never expect much from continental breakfast. Good coffee could also be had around the corner on Polk at the Royal Ground, and 1/2 way decent bagels at the San Francisco Bagelry (Polk as well). The 20 something crowd would like the proximity of this hotel to the bars. Perhaps not as ideal for families with younger kids (no pool, no green space to run around), but this is an urban area after all.

<Content>A Great Place to Stay in San Francisco After doing much research on the internet looking for a hotel to stay for our 3 nights in San Francisco that offered a good location, reasonable price, inclusive car parking and previous good reviews, we selected the Castle Inn as this seemed to tick all the boxes. <Author>lukabrasi007
<Content>It's all you really need... First, what Castle Inn is not...Castle Inn is not the Ritz. Do not expect to be pampered or receive room service. However, if you want a decent hotel at a very reasonable price, then Castle Inn is the place. It's closer to a Red Roof Inn/Motel 6 but is WELL WORTH the price. I'd stay there again in a heartbeat and suggest it to anyone wanting to stay in SF.Pros: Great location in the interesting and safe neighborhood of Russian Hill, about 2 blocks from different 3 bus lines (get used to taking the bus...they're safe and convenient), about 1-2 blocks from restaurants and boutiques, not a lot of hills in this area, free parking (HUGE benefit), microwave and fridge in the room, clean, excellent service via internet liason (Varsa), helpful front office (Marshall), and the City tour we booked through Varsa and Tower Tours was well worth the price.Cons: Parking (although free) is a little tight...but so is the rest of San Francisco, our king bed was pretty uncomfortable...my shoulder hurt and my wife's back hurt after a couple of nights, we had some noisy neighbors above us one night around midnight and it took the front office a little while to respond to it. All in all, no major problems with Castle Inn. One negative thing to keep in mind about San Francisco: it is very expensive. Expect to pay $40-$50 for a tasty, but otherwise average meal. (I don't care what Zagat or other restaurant guides say...expect to pay more)Gas was $3.70/gallon. It won't be a cheap trip...but it is totally worth it.We had a great experience at Castle Inn. I shopped around quite a bit before booking my room and I honestly feel that this is the best value in the City. Other discount hotels charge anywhere from $10-30 a day for parking, so factor that in before choosing. Also other discount hotels that I looked at booking a room are in semi-rough neighborhoods. Castle Inn is in a very residential area (which I really enjoyed) but is just a 5 or 10 minute bus ride to almost anywhere in the city. Also, I really can't say enough nice things about Varsa (internet liason). She was very helpful and answered even the most mundane questions I had about the city. She's a real San Francisco ambassador. I give Castle Inn a 4 out of 5 and a hearty recommendation.

<Author>ttoo
<Content>A great find My family decided to try the Castle inn March 16-20 after reading a review in a tour book and checking Trip Advisor and finding generallygreat reviews. We were very satisfied and were lucky to have Varsa onsight the entire time of our stay as she was genuinely friendly andinformative about how to see the sights in the city, where to buy themuni pass, etc. Many tourists near the wharf asked where I got the convienent, small map she provided and she also provided another one for my young son who loves to have his own copy. This is not a fancy place- furnishings were on par with Days Inn type chain but the rate was great for our family (as cheap as $99/night during the week if you book directly from their website) and included free parking and free continental breakfast which easily saved us $400 plus from the places I was looking at near the wharf area. We had room 225 which was midway back from street with rooms above and below and although we could hear street and other noise as we had the air conditioning off during our stay, it wasn't excessive nor did it intrude our sleep. You are in a city. My kids loved to go to the office to retrieve a tray of food in the morning and talk to Varsa (you have to eat in your room as the office isn't big enough to eat there) and we felt the place was safe enough to let them go off by themselves this distance. There are restaurants and Walgreens, etc. within a half block on Polk Street which was convienent but not intrusive. We got popcorn and drinks to store in fridge/microwave provided in each room. The beds were rather soft but it was very clean and the linens were better than average. Enjoyed staying away from the massesdown near the wharf but within 2 blocks of the cable car or a 20 min walk to this area. Walked around at night and never felt uneasy. Again, Varsa was very kind- provided postcard stamps and looked up an address for us on the internet and the hours of business for another attraction. We arrived rather late (after the posted office hours of 11pm) but had called a week ahead to confirm that we would be accomodated and also enroute and they waited up for us. It was a great choice for our first visit to SF and would have no qualms aboutstaying at the Castle again for this princess! Thank you trip advisorcontributors for this find!

<Author>apothecary
<Content>Do not trust the Castle Inn The Castle Inn was terrible! I had booked through Expedia to stay here for a few days last April. Despite the fact that it was more or less a motel, I was initially swayed by all of the great reviews on this site.I had emailed the hotel a couple of days prior to my arrival to confirm everything which is usually what I do when I book through a 3rd party like Expedia or Orbitz. I was told everything was on target. To be noted, when I booked a few months prior through Expedia, I booked at an Expedia special rate which meant that my credit card was charged for the whole stay immedicately on booking.When we arrived at the Castle after a drive from Monterrey, we stopped at the office to check in and were greeted by a very unpleasant person. She was pleasant until I told her my name, and then her expression changed. It was as if she was hoping we were not showing up. At first she told us that they had no idea we were coming. When I showed her my paid in full confirmation from Expedia and the email from the hotel stating that they were expecting us, she then said that they were overbooked and could not accommodate us, even though our reservations were guaranteed and we were NOT a late arrival. Funny that she forgot about us but they didn't forget to collect the money from our booking months before. She then got on the phone and came back and told us that they would put us up at a sister hotel that was nice than theirs at no extra charge.Since we had never been to San Francisco and had no other options at this point, we went to the sister hotel (Francisco Bay Inn). It was terrible, did not have the same rating or accommodations as the Castle Inn, was located in a crappy, ghetto area and had loud truck noise constantly making it impossible to sleep. To top things off, it was dirty and I got stuck in their crappy elevator for 2 hours until they finally decided to call the elevator repair company. The cost for this hotel on Expedia when I checked was $50 less per night! I called Expedia to complain and they said the 2 hotels should be equivalent in accommodations so all they could do was give me a $50 coupon toward my next booking with them. I did call my credit card to file a complaint.Based on this, I would not trust the Castle Inn and their shady bait and switch system. I should have posted this review months ago but kind of forgot about trip advisor. The fact that I am this upset almost 1 year later should be warning to you!

<Author>Lucreciamott
<Content>Nice place, nice price, good location We stayed at the Castle Inn in February after reading the reviews and we were not disappointed. We were 3 people in 2 rooms. Both were clean and big (specially for European standards), with TV, fridge, microwave and iron. The noise from the traffic did not bother us at all, although you could hear the cars passing by. We never made it to breakfast since it was very early but, as others said, there are plenty of places for that in Polk St. Staff were very friendly and helpful. The free parking was great. As for the location, we walked to Fisherman's Wharf easily (that's all downhill from the hotel) and even to Lombard St (but you have to literally climb up a hill for that!). The area is very nice and quiet. Someone complained in another review about the noise from the nightclubs and from the people in other rooms. We stayed at the Castle Inn 12 nights in total (9 when we arrived to the States and 3 before we left) using 4 different rooms and we never had any problems with any noise.I would highly recommend this hotel to anyone who wants a budget place in a nice area.

<Author>RockDoctor
<Content>Doesn't get better at the price in SF Had an excellent three-night stay at the Castle in Feb. All the reviews are spot on - this place is great value. You're in a great SAFE location, close to everything you need and public transport almost at the door for further afield. Polk St is pretty funky and has a handy supermarket and the Real Food store is tops for healthy food options. Room was good - reasonable size, very clean and well serviced. Free wireless internet, tea/coffee, basic brekkie all thrown in! Great value given the great rates you can get booking direct.As for location, some reviews have been scathing, but I can't imagine why. Seemed very safe, even late at night, unlike Union Square/Market areas which get rapidly seedy as you stray from the most major shopping areas. Would recommend this location based on feeling safe and also how easy it is to get to everywhere else you might want to see in San Fran. US$18 3-day pass for MUNI is all you need to see it all, bargain.Hosts are friendly and the check-in blurb is worth paying attention to, these guys know their city and advise well.In summary, great value property in a good area of the city with welcoming and friendly hosts. Would recommend unreservedly for value-for-money in San Fran. (The hotel website should probably include a photo of the more motel-style accommodation at the back which forms a large part of this hotel though.)

<Content>Extremely good value for San Francisco We chose the Castle Inn due to its incredible value, more than anything as well as for its safe location. <Author>riseandshine
<Content>What a lovely place As many others (I suspect), me and my girlfriend came across Castle Inn through the many great reviews on tripadvisor, and we were not disappointed.We stayed there for a total of seven days, and during that time we stayed in two seperate rooms. Both of them were in excellent condition, and, importantly, squeaky clean. You get free wireless internet (which, except for a minor glitches, worked flawlessly and fast compared to other (major) hotel networks I've tried), and you get many, many TV channels - if that means anything to you.The staff is as friendly as they get, and the location is marvellous. Lots of restaurants nearby (including the ones in Italian district), and a very relaxed, cosy atmosphere characterizes the neigborhood. It's a quite hilly area, so expect to use either bus or cable car, which both pass by in close approximity to the motel.If you want to do some major shopping (around Union Square, for example), you will probably want to use public transport. You could walk on a warm day, but don't overestimate your physical fitness when you're going back again ...Also, Castle Inn is very good value for money. We payed about $100 a night, and considering the large rooms, the service and the extras like wireless internet and TV selection, we can't complain.If you expect to get a proper breakfast, though, you should probably visit any of the nearby cafes or even Walgreens (for some decent sandwiches). The one in Castle Inn is a bit on the sugary side, but the coffee is great! :)

<Author>Aged_Travellers
<Content>Good Location, Friendly Staff After reading encouraging reviews of this hotel on Trip Advisor we decided to give it a try - a good choice. Although the location isn't central, it is convenient for cable cars and buses and is within walking distance of Fisherman's Wharf - hotel reception gave us details of transport links. Reception staff were extremely friendly and very helpful. An added bonus was the free parking. The room was spacious and clean although a little tired, perhaps some refurbishment would help. The bed was large and very comfortable. An adequate breakfast was included in the nightly rate. There were numerous shops and restaurants in the next street.Although close to busy roads and the Broadway Tunnel, we were never disturbed by traffic noise. I would recommend the Castle Inn to anyone wanting a decent hotel in San Francisco at a reasonable price.

<Author>JandJUk
<Content>A good find This is a very nice place. First impression might be that it's a little 'faded' but actually, it's fine - warm, clean, fairly quiet, not too far from things, good value and, above all, the most friendly and helpful staff you could wish to encounter anywhere. Nothing is too much trouble, you feel. We stayed at the start and end of a trip to California and each time, the different members of the desk team ensured I had a map, any other info I might need, and brought to my attention the areas they considered potentially unsafe (not nearby). Unwittingly, we went to collect breakfast a bit late - it had been put away, but they got stuff out for us, with no sense of inconvenience. And when a staff member saw us arrive quite late at night to find the car park full, he came out and moved his car so that we could have a space. I'd definitely stay there again on another trip

<Author>Karla-8
<Content>no point in staying here I fell for all the wonderful reviews as well, wrongly assuming the couple negative ones must have been flukes, but I won't make that mistake again. We tried to check out after the 1st night but would have been penalized with a stiff cancellation fee so we stayed, begrudgingly, knowing we'd be moving on to better shortly. (We were returning to San Francisco the following weekend and staying elsewhere). Helpful Hint: don't bother complaining to the clerk/reservationist, she has an answer for everything. What blew me away though, was with the information readily available on the Internet, why would you risk future business by keeping an unhappy customer? Smarter business would be to let them go so they could at least report that the situation was handled reasonably and satisfactorily. It was very annoying. We were told (with a smile) that we expect people to do their research 1st. So that's why I'm writing my 1st review ever, so the next family doesn't have to hear that line. Very frustrating for me as I'm a research freak, but the reservationist/desk clerk claimed it was a great place for toddlers, great location, easy to get around, etc. Definitely not true! Anyway, the location is depressing both inside and out. There is no convenient way to get around, unless you like standing in the rain waiting for buses and taxis, the latter of which are hard to come by. Not at all advisable with a toddler. The only thing it has going for it is free parking, but one doesn't need a car in the city anyway. Oh, and it's also very noisy at night. The walls are thin and the plumbing loud! Both inside and outside noise through the night. I brought earplugs but my husband didn't get much sleep.The bottom line is, there's just no point in staying here. There are so many options with better locations and similar prices, with lobbies, amenities and so much more. For what we paid in taxis we could have stayed in a 4 star hotel in a great location with everything in walking distance. Our friends stayed at the Marriott Parc 55 for half the price we were paying. It's just not worth the frustration.

<Author>mambo69cat
<Content>GREAT STAY We have just returned home to England from California and we stayed for 4 nights at the castle inn during that time. We choose it after reading reviews on this website and booked through Expedia. ( It is probably cheaper to book direct with hindsight). Its in a lovely position just below Nob Hill, around Russian Hill, on the corner of Van Ness and Broadway. The area is very safe and in Polk street, just over the road, there are a few nice restaurants, cafes and the inevitable Walgreens. If you like Chinese food, halfway down Polk Street on the left from the hotel, there is a little Chinese restaurant/take away, nothing posh, but the food was beautiful - fresh cooked to order and really reasonable priced - try the plum wine at $2.50 per glass. Its called Andy's.Back to Castle Inn - lots of good free parking, pleasant hosts, very comfortable, clean rooms with the usual facilities. Comfortable beds with pastel shade bedlinen. Coffee/tea available all day in the small reception, plus there is a coffee maker in room. There is a complimentary continental breakfast - fruit, muffins, danish, etc. which you take up to your room on a tray.All in all, would definitely stay there again. We bought a 3 day pass that we could use on street cars, trams, buses and metro for just $18 each. (its $5 for just one journey on a street car), and we really had our value over 3 days.

We honestly really enjoyed our stay and would recommend it to anyone who wants to experience San Francisco for the first time and has no need for flashy accomodations. When we go back to San Fran, I will be sure to stay there again.

<Author>Thommy2000
<Content>Great Place, Great Neighborhood I think the Castle Inn is a very clean and well run hotel. It's not a Sheraton or a Hilton by all means, but the rooms are clean and the surrounding neighborhood is safe enough to walk at any time of the day. Marshall was an excellent host who gave us the DL (down low) on the best areas of San Francisco. The free parking was a plus because parking in the city is a big hassle. Leave your car in the garage and take public transportation. I also suggest that you explore the surrounding neighborhood especially along Polk Street. There's an excellent wine store (William Cross), a great cheese store, a great coffee shop (Peets) and the best sports bar/pub in SF (Green's). It was an easy walk to the wharf without too many steep hills, as a matter of fact, we could never get a cab at the wharf and had to walk back late at night several times with no problems, heck after all the food we ate we needed the exercise anyway. All in all the Castle Inn is the best hotel you'll find in the city for the money and safety. Thanks for having us!

<Author>Andrew_McQuilly
<Content>A good choice in San Francisco Arriving in your room at the Castle Inn you might find yourself a little disappointed. The room is modestly sized, and the chances are you'll have a view of the walkway connecting the rooms which overlook the courtyard (car park). However, this place has plenty of good things going for it and proved to be an excellent option for our stay in San Francisco.The greeting was fantastic. After being given the keys to our room we were invited back to reception where the receptionist provided us with books and maps of the city, along with superb advice as to where to go and what to see.Although a little small, the room was spotless and very well decorated. The shower head had a number of interesting settings, including the pulse massage which was well appreciated after being enveloped in the cold SF fog. The 'kitchen' area was a little odd, comprising a microwave, coffee maker and fridge, but little in the way of utensils. This isn't a complaint as the facilities were well appreciated, rather it's an observation.The Inn stands just off highway 101, which meant that it was easy for me as a tourist to find, and to get back on to to reach the airport on the final day of my stay.A short walk around the corner on to Polk Street finds you among a good range of good quality coffee shops, bars and restaurants, as well as an organic market and chilled food takeaway which did a fantastic won ton salad. There is little other accomodation in this area so it feels like you are living among the locals. Unfortunately we weren't told about the free breakfast, but I think this was our gain as we found a fantastic 'boulangerie' nearby selling a delicious range of pastries and fantastic coffee.Although this hotel isn't in the middle of the tourist hustle, it is only a fifteen minute walk from Fisherman's Wharf. If you want to stay somewhere residential, away from the tourists, but on the doorstep of the sights, then as long as you keep your expectations realistic the Castle Inn shouldn't disappoint.

<Author>razzrazz
<Content>It's ok When we arrived I was a bit disappointed, not sure what I was expecting but all the rooms face down into a courtyard. Someone else described it more motor inn than motel/hotel  I would have to agree. Obvious plus, they don't charge extra for parking your car there like many other hotels. The staff is extremely friendly, well informed  more than willing to help you anyway they can. The room was very clean and roomy except for the bathroom area. The bathroom is the size of a closet and I'm not a big person  nowhere to put anything once inside. The sink is outside but not much room there either. It's a solid 15 min. walk downhill to the Wharf  that's the beginning of the Wharf, it will take you another 10 mins. to walk, let's say to the pier for Alcatraz - it's pretty much all uphill back - best to take the bus or trolly - both leave you near the hotel. I'd skip the continental breakfast, nothing special, some fruit, no fresh muffins - packaged stuff - would have been nice to have some real milk or cream for coffee/tea as opposed to powdered. <Content>Great location, friendly staff We stayed at the Castle Inn for 5 nights and found the place to be exactly as others had described. The staff were very helpful and friendly and the location was great for exploring the city. Room was comfortable and the breakfast although only light was really convenient. <Author>jgh
<Content>Lives Up To Its Reputation We chose Castle Inn for our three night stay in San Francisco based on the excellent reviews on tripadvisor.com. I am happy to report that the positive reviews are right on the money. We actually arrived two hours prior to check in time and were given a room right away. We stayed in #339, which is the last room on the top floor. Very quiet since no other guests walk by the room. Parking was always available. Check in and out went extremely smoothly. Owners and staff were knowledgeable and very friendly. Our room was basic, similar to La Quinta, but was very clean and had everything we needed. The location was ideal for visiting all the tourist spots, and there is a Starbucks right around the corner on Polk. We rode the cable car/bus one day and drove the next day. We much preferred having our car and did not have difficulty finding parking. We paid about the same for two all day bus passes as we did for parking the next day. We highly recommend Castle Inn! The total cost was approximately half of staying at the better known chains.

<Author>HappyTraveler42
<Content>Great Value in San Fran Agree heartily with many of the other reviewers of the Castle. It's a great value spot in San Francisco. Not fancy but clean, comfortable beds, free parking, well located and good service by the owners.Please ask the proprietors for restaurant advice. We ate at three of their recommendations (Chinese, Mexican and burgers) in the neighborhood and had great food at very reasonable prices. Much better quality and value than the places down by the Wharf.Strongly recommend buying the public transportation pass. We did the three day pass and you can use the trains, buses or cable cars. Saves alot of time and energy instead of battling SF's famous hills. And don't wait in the often long lines at the beginning of the cable car routes. Walk up a stop and grab a spot - they don't fill the cars to capacity at the origin.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Place for A Great Price My wife and I planned our first trip to San Francisco and Napa valley and used TripAdvisor as one of our main research tools. We opted to stay at the Castle Inn after reading numerous reviews and checking out prices. All I can say is that our visit lived up to our expectations. The Castle Inn was clean and centrally located to many of the attractions we were interested in visiting. While researching places to stay, I was impressed with the prior reviews of this location as well as the fact that the GM personally responded to one of the only negative reviews posted. When we checked in, I was pleased with the exceptional 'customer service' we received. Without inquiry, we were provided with everything we could possibly need to navigate the city. We received a map of the city, local bus and trolley routes as well as first hand advice on which roads to take and places of interest. This type of service was routine during our visit. Interestingly enough, on one of the days we were visiting, the hotel management was replacing the room furniture. Let me tell you, it was a recipe for disaster when you consider that a large moving truck had to be parked in front of the hotel and the movers needed to complete this task in a three level hotel without disturbing guests. Personally, I was pleased with how the process went. The night before the move, the GM called us to advise what was going to happen and what we should expect. Although the movers were later than expected, I was completely satisfied with the manner in which our furniture swap was handled. The pictures currently available on this site appear to have the older furniture. The new furniture is much lighter in color.A few other notable benefits of this location include free parking (which is very impressive when you look at other hotels), an abundance of restaurants nearby and the ability to walk to locations such as the Fisherman's Wharf, Chinatown, Coit Tower, Lombard St, and Union Square. Please note that I indicated the ability to walk to these locations. A few are a good 2 mile + walk so please take that into consideration. If you are thinking about staying at the Castle Inn, please be aware this isn't similar to a Marriott or a Sheraton. It isn't nearly as plush. If you are the type of traveler that is looking for a reasonable place to stay where you can ask the hotel staff for advice or suggestions, then the Castle Inn is likely for you. I really felt like they took an interest in my stay and wanted repeat business.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Terrific hotel for families We stayed at The Castle for three nights in mid-June (two parents, one 6-year-old, one 12-year-old). Like other reviewers, I certainly agree that the hotel was above average in cleanliness (I recently stayed at a 5 star hotel in Atlanta and The Castle's rooms were cleaner), there was ample parking and the location is perfect when you're not driving. We were able to catch the bus at a stop that was a minute away, there were two coffee houses and a bagel shop around the corner and lots of local flavor.But what impressed me the most was the people who worked at the Castle Inn. Our flight from Houston was delayed by three hours so when we got to the Castle, we had 30 minutes to check in and make it to our Alcatraz tour -- Varsa immediately worked with me to check us in while another Castle employee (I'm sorry that I didn't catch his name) explained to my husband how to get to the tour and answered all his questions. Throughout our stay, Varsa was always willing to answer our questions -- she gave us lots of directions, recommended local restaurants and always had a smile on her face. When we asked about a place she hadn't visited, she asked us about it when we got back not only because she said she'd always thought of visiting but so she'd have information if a future guest asked. Clean, comfortable rooms, great prices and extraordinarly friendly staff make the Castle Inn a gem of a hotel. I've already recommended the Castle Inn to a friend and we certainly will stay here again!

<Content>Honeymoon Highlight We arrived late on Tuesday June 20th and stayed 3 nights at the beginning of our 8 night, 7 day honeymoon to San Francisco and Sonoma Valley. Sy met us at about midnight and immediately began providing extremely useful information. Varsa was just as helpful the next day. They provided us with a cheat sheet of directions to all the key tourist sites and provided us with excellent restaurant recommendations within the area that were not tourist traps. We tried 3 of them and were very pleased. Tai Chi (Polk and Broadway) was a Hunan Mandarin restaurant that was out of this world. Hyde Street Seafood House was incredible for (wait for it -) seafood. Street on Polk has wonderful ambience. $2 Happy Hour (Thursdays and Fridays 5 to 9 p.m.) at Rouge (Polk and Broadway) was great too. The Polk Street/Russian Hill area is an incredible district. Castle Inn is right in the middle of it and within walking distance to Fisherman's Wharf, Lombard Street (the Crooked Street), Nob Hill and North Beach.The hotel is great value for money. The room was one of the cleanest we have ever stayed in and was very quiet (we were near the back of the hotel). We greatly appreciated the amazing personal concierge service from Sy and Varsa! We highly recommend this hotel.

Plenty of water pressure and hot water. * Marshall in the front desk was really helpful with directions and telling us where to go in San Fran. He also drew an area on the map and told us not to go there (Tenderloin). The only downside was he was suffering from an ear infection when we were there so he was a bit grumpy.* The location is fantastic, especially for budget travellers who need facilities like laundromats and internet (both are within a two minute walk of the hotel). Marshall also gives you a sheet explaining all the main attractions and how to access them via bus/tram. This piece of paper was my bible for the week. What a great idea!There were a couple of negatives:* Our room was facing the street and it can get a bit noisy in the early hours. I kept getting woken up by drunk guys stumbling home.* Also, we came back to our room at around midday one day to find a couple of workmen in our room changing the blinds. We weren't warned that this was going to happen so we were a bit disappointed (especially since we weren't gone long so we left our valuables there). Let me stress that nothing went missing though, and the workmen were very apologetic for their intrusion.Still, I'd recommend this hotel. It can be a bit daunting when selecting a hotel in San Francisco, particularly with all the hullaballoo about the dangers of the Tenderloin. If you in any way concerned about that, stay here. It's a nice part of town with nice eateries within five minutes walk.  
<Date>Jun 26, 2006

<Author>Woodpecker-47
<Content>Great stay!! We stayed here in April with our 2 older kids and would really recommend it. We stayed 3 nights in a family suite (don't know if they have more than one) and booked directly with the hotel. Varsa was so helpful when we arrived and supplied us with maps and recommended restaurants and shopping areas to us. The accomodation was very clean and consisted of a large living room with double bed, sofas  TV and off there was a short corridor with another double bedroom (with TV) a bathroom, plus a large walk in closet with fridge, microwave and coffee maker ( there were no proper cooking facilities though). The main bedroom/living room faced the street but we weren't bothered by the traffic noise and the other bedroom faced onto the external walkway/courtyard and was much quieter. There was a basic continental breakfast available until around 9am from the front office that you could take back to your room on a tray but lots of very good restaurants were available within a few minutes walk of the hotel. Everything was within 30 minutes walking distance (Wharf, Union square, China town) but we usually used public transport to get us back. We weren't in the room that much (too much to see and do in SF!) but when we were, there was enough space for all of us and would stay there again.

<Author>Jaybyrd1
<Content>Loved the Castle Inn The Castle Inn is a great place to stay in San Francisco. We spent a couple of nights at the Castle Inn on a recent trip to the San Francisco area. The hosts, Arlene and Marshall were very pleasant and helpful. Our flight arrived extremely late and we did not get to the hotel until long after the front desk normally would have closed. <Author>jng06
<Content>Perfect for our vacation I am a picky traveler and I usually stick to big hotel chains that I know and that are cookie cutter consistent. I was a little leery about choosing the Castle Inn for our brief (3 and 1/2 day) trip, but I was put off by the prices of the big chains in Fishermans Wharf (and by the big parking fees, since we'd be bringing a car for the non-San Francisco part of our trip).I am pleased to say that the Castle Inn is as good as reported by prevous Trip Advisor reviewers. I NEVER would have chosen it from it's appearance on the street (I am a little of a hotel snob and I really like a showy marble foyer). Not choosing this hotel would be a mistake, however. The foyer/office is tiny but is filled with the gracious presence of Marshall and Arlene. We arrived 5 hours prior to check-in time but it was no problem to leave our car in the very safe and covered parking area while we went out and started to explore the city. Marshall spent a good 15 minutes with us going over a map with many suggestions for San Francisco first-timers, including how to get around on the public transportation. The hotel (?motel) was about a 2-3 block walk to the cable car route.Our room was not fancy-fancy, but very clean and perfect for our family of 2 adults and 2 teens. There was no view, but we were going to San Fran to get out and see the views ourselves, not sit in a hotel and look out the window.The breakfast was tiny, but got us going - basically packaged muffins, danish, granola bars, fruit, coffee and juice.I/we would definitely come here again. I thank the Trip Advisor reviewers for helping me find a gem that I never would have found by myself.

<Author>luv2cruisegirl
<Content>Beware! After reserving a room six months in advance via the telephone we arrived at the Castle Inn only to find out that they gave our room away. We chose the Castle Inn based on all the reviews from TripAdvisor. I called Castle Inn twice to confirm my reservations. On both occasions the receptionist was in a hurry and the phone conversations ended fast. One week before our reservation and just before getting on our cruise in LA I called one more time to confirm, yes, we will see you then. After taking the Super Shuttle to the Castle Inn from Oakland Airport (we arrived at the Castle Inn at 3:00 p.m.) we were stunned to find out they gave our room away! What good is having a confirmation number if it doesn't mean they have a room for you. We were told that they tried to contact us, funny we were on a cruise with no phone! Lucky for us we ended up at the Nob Hill Motor Inn just around the corner, by far a better facility for the same price! My advice to everyone, Confirm, Confirm and re-confirm and don't let the hurried receptionist off the phone until you have verified all telephone numbers and credit card numbers with them or you could wind up with just a confirmation number and no room!

<Author>toereesa
<Content>Perfect Location and Price The Castle Inn hotel is a perfect base camp for touring San Franscisco. It is located in a wonderful and safe neighborhood with lots of local restaurants and entertainment. It is in walking distance of the Fisherman's Warves, North Beach (Little Italy and China town), Ghiradelli Square, Lombard Street, Coit Tower, etc. The owners were extremely helpful providing you with tourist info and maps explaining how to get everywhere using the public transportation. The rooms were clean and large with beds that were quite comfy. The bathroom was OK in size with a great showerhead. The only drawback about the hotel are the thin walls. You can hear normal toned conversations taking place next door. But this really wasn't a problem since people respected the quiet hours. For the price, location, and hospitality, you can't go wrong. I would definately go back to Castle Inn.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Hotel 鈥?Great Location-Wonderful Value! We really enjoyed our stay at the Castle Inn! We were there for 4 nights and enjoyed it more than our stays at much more expensive places. What made it special were the attitudes of the innkeepers! They all were friendly, helpful, and just enjoyable to talk to. They set up our tours of San Francisco, plus arranged for airport transfers. They were always available to answer questions, provide maps, and give advice. This certainly saved us a lot of money, time, and effort! As far as location, we thought it was great. Bus lines run on either side, and the Cable Car was several blocks over. Parking is free 鈥?a great thing to find in San Francisco. There were many good restaurants, shops, coffee shops, and a grocery store within an easy walk. Our room was large with a King Size bed (extremely comfortable), refrigerator, microwave, coffee maker, TV, table and chairs. There was also an iron and board. The shower had plenty of power, and everything was very clean and well maintained! Breakfast was what we expected: juice, yogurt, sweet rolls, muffins, a selection of granola bars, fresh fruit. We could just load up our tray and eat in our room. There was always hot water in the office for Tea, Hot Chocolate, or Instant coffee, and they were happy to provide extra coffee for the coffeemaker (unlike many much more expensive hotels). We will definitely stay here on our next trip to SF.

<Content>Great Value! Great Location! My wife and I recently were looking for a nice yet economic place to stay in the San Francisco area. <Author>wurly_monster
<Content>Best value and service OK, this is my third stay in San Francisco. I've stayed in 3 hotels and each time I've located a better hotel - Best Western Americania - dodgy location; Hotel Adagio - still a bit of a dodgy location, but a bit more expensive than the Castle Inn.... Anyway, the Castle Inn is by far the best of these 3. And the hotel's area is a lot safer than the areas around Union Square and City Hall - where many other hotels are located. Once you get to San Francisco you'll understand this statement better - there are a lot of crazy people who approach you in the street in this city - unlike other major western cities (NY, London, Paris, Tokyo etc). Homelessness is out of control.The hotel room was massive - with a living area space to eat, and a decent sized bathroom. The service, as noted by others here, is exceptional.While it is a bit of a hike to get down to Union Square - a walk and bus, or a walk and cable car (if you can get on), the hotel is located in a nice area of Nob Hill and is walkable to Fisherman's Wharf etc.If I ever return to San Francisco, I would come back to the Castle Inn.

<Author>brenny
<Content>Lived up to Expectations We have just returned from a skiing holiday at Lake Tahoe with 3 days in San Francisco before returning home. Our accommodation at Tahoe was booked through the travel agent but we decided to go it alone with the accommodation in San Francisco. Having pored over the Tripadvisor reviews we decided on the Castle Inn. We were not disappointed. After having flight delays, and baggage lost, we finally arrived at the Castle Inn. Varsa was behind the desk at reception with her ever-smiling face. She is always cheery, has a wealth of information, and has prepared a printed sheet of well known attractions and how to get to them using public transport. The room was large and very clean. There was ample room to put skis, boots, bags and not even notice they were there. We had a king size bed, cable television, more than adequate heating, and plenty of very hot water.There is also a microwave and frig in the room. It is a 10 minute walk to Fisherman's Wharf, although a bit hilly on the way back. The area is very safe, which was a big factor in choosing this hotel. There are quite a few little restaurants close by. Breakfast, with a choice of coffee, several fruit, yoghurt, pastries and breakfast bars, is included and available at reception. We didn't have a car, but there is also free parking. Having not been to San Francisco for almost 10 years, our only regret was that we didn't have longer there. This hotel is not the Hilton, but it is a homely, clean, roomy hotel at much less than Hilton prices. You would have to be incredibly fussy, or very unlucky, to be disappointed.

<Author>captcor
<Content>Very nice place We spent 3 nights in the Castle Inn's only suite. It is not a fancy hotel but was perfect for four people (two adults with two teenagers). The suite is more like an apartment and has two good sized clean rooms each with a king sized bed. There is a good sized bath and huge walk-in closet. The larger of the rooms also had two sofas and two chairs. The second room is off of a hallway--good for privacy. The suite has a small refrigerator with separate freezer, microwave, iron and board. We used a roll-away in the larger room for one of the teenagers. It was far better than the usual roll-away. More like a twin bed on wheels. The cost of the suite was far less than two separate rooms would have been and if we found two rooms at another hotel for what we paid for the suite, I am sure that they would not be nearly as nice. The Castle Inn is located in the Russian Hill area of the city, a vibrant and convenient neighborhood with many varied restaurants within a few block walk. We felt more like we were living like locals than staying at a hotel. The free covered parking is a big plus. Cable cars are nearby, only 21/2 blocks. We bought 3 day city transportation passes at $18 each and used them a lot, a bargain particularly since the cable cars are otherwise $5/ride. Fisherman's wharf was a pleasant walk and also a great cable car ride away. Desk staff could not have been nicer or more helpful. Altogether, the Casle Inn is a fine choice.

<Author>shriken
<Content>loved it Excellent location; at VanNess and Broadway provides *easy* bus and taxi access, very short (2 1/2 blocks) walk to cable car line. Very safe section of town. The way the place is laid out, the rooms lie behind the office and elevator and such, so things tend to be quiet (you're in a big city here folks, so you do get fire engines and such!) The staff went way way way out of their way to make us feel at home, to help us find things and to get around. Bathroom (toilet/shower) was small but completely clean and functional. The micro/fridge, sink, mirror/vanity area was a roomy space separate from the toilet. Posted photos here on trip advisor from other reviews are legit representations. If you have a car (I don't recommend a car in SanFran) their off street parking is simply AMAZING.

<Author>Claire55812
<Content>We liked the Castle Inn, though it wasn't perfect Three of us stayed at the Castle Inn last week after two nights at the Sheraton on Fisherman's Wharf. In terms of location, we much preferred the Castle Inn, the neighborhood it's located in is such a great place to dine, walk around, have coffee, and window-shop. It's much more of the real SF than Fisherman's Wharf, which is like Disneyland. It's also a few blocks from the cable car, so it was pretty easy to take the cable cars downtown, and we rode the cable cars as much as we could. In terms of the room itself, the Sheraton was of course fancier digs, but we liked our room fine, it had 2 Queen beds, and it was perfectly fine for our needs. And they were generous with towels.As everybody agrees, Versa is the best. She was so friendly, so helpful with restaurant recommendations and transportation advice. I really liked her a lot, she really made our stay a pleasant one,she's that place's #1 draw. We stayed at the Castle Inn over New Year's weekend, so prices were jacked up. I think if I had to pay top dollar like I did for that weekend, I'd stay somewhere nicer and closer to the action. But we did get free parking, and that was very helpful, and I appreciated being able to use my laptop in the room to cruise the net and read my email.The only two things that bothered me about our stay at the Castle Inn were: 1. we asked them if we could leave our suitcases there after checking out since we had a midnight flight. They said yes, and we thought they'd put our luggage behind the desk or in some other secure location. When we came bsck after a day of sightseeing, our luggage was exactly where we had left it, in the small front office, next to the door. I was glad that I had kept my laptop with me, or I really would have been upset. Anyone could have walked off with our stuff. Also 2. When we came back to the hotel after dinner to retrieve our luggage and get to SFO, we asked the owner, Marsh, to call us a cab. He suggested instead that we take a limo that his friend drives, his friend was right there, it'd cost us $50, not much more than a cab, he said (our cab from SFO to Fisherman's Wharf a week before had cost us $42 plus tip). We felt pressured to take the limo, even though it cost more than the cab, and we're not rolling in cash. And, I found out later, I could have gotten a limo for $40--there was an advertisement in the Bay Area Guide for a limo to the airport for $39. Next time, I'll make my plans for transportation to the airport ahead of time, so I don't find myself in that kind of a situation again. It was fine riding in the limo, (sedan), but I could have planned better and saved some money, instead of feeling like I had to take this guy up on his offer of having his friend take us to the airport.Overall, we liked the Castle Inn, it's a perfectly nice motel with a very competent and helpful manager (Versa) in a super neighborhood with great coffeehouses (like Royal Grounds) and restaurants (like Yabbies and the Hyde St. Seafood Bistro).

<Author>Vickie_Bernie
<Content>Great Place, Great Price, Great Staff, But... Well so much good had been said about this hotel I knew we would be happy staying here. It was easy to find, parking for free is a bonus and boy oh boy was Versa a wealth of information! She was always smiling, and ready with any questions. Water in the shower went from cold to hot and back again. All in all it was adequate for what we needed. The price was certainly good. But I don't think I would stay here again, I may need to pay more and get more.
