<Author>midas
<Content>Nice hotel , Exceptional service At first sight the Castle Inn was a bit disappointing, nothing really Castle-like about its appearance! But haven鈥檛 all the wise people told us 鈥?appearances are deceptive! That is the adage that best applies to the Castle Inn, it is the hidden jewel of SFO. The rooms were surprisingly spacious (by SFO standards); super clean, well lit and very tastefully decorated. The view from the windows was amazing. And what can I say about Varsa, she was so helpful and so considerate. She was always well equipped with maps, directions, and all kinds of information. And always prompt to provide local tips and suggestions.The motel is located in a very safe and well-lit area, we were out till midnight and never felt uncomfortable. All the attractions are within close walking distances, we walked everywhere (and we are really lazy people)! Polk Street is dotted with quaint shops, we could have spent hours browsing there. The area also offers a multitude of eating-places nearby, offering a variety of world cuisines. The Indian restaurant round the corner has amazing food! Our only regret, wish we could spend more time in SFO!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great place to stay We stayed at the Castle Inn for 6 nights. We made our booking based on reviews and we were not disappointed. We booked direct with the hotel so even before we got there Varsa had contacted us with details of trips and things to do. We booked the City Tour and the Wine Country Tour. Both were excellent. Varsa also advised us to book our trip to Alcatraz in advance and that was good advice. We did the night tour - fabulous. Back to the Castle Inn - our room was spacious and spotlessly clean. Having a fridge is a bonus. We didn't have any problems with noise. The location is great. We walked everywhere but there's plenty of public transport if the hills get too much. The local restaurants are great. We particularly enjoyed the Rex Cafe for Sunday Brunch and Yabbie's for seafood. Both are on Polk Street just round the corner. The hotel provides coffee and pastries for breakfast but we liked to pick up fresh bagels from the Bagelry which is also on Polk Street. The Castle Inn offers great value, friendly service and a perfect location.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great value and location! We chose the Castle Inn after reading all the positive reviews on this site. Four of us stayed in a room with two queen-sized beds and it had everything we needed including a TV, microwave, and fridge. The breakfast provided included coffee, tea, orange juice, yogurt, fruit, danish and muffins and gave us a good start to the day. If you're looking for excellent value for money the Castle Inn meets the bill - it's a decent place to stay at a great location as it's only a short walk to Fisherman's Wharf. The staff were very helpful, providing us with bus info and a map, giving suggestions on where to eat and ordering us a taxi when we left the hotel to return home. Before our stay, Varsa was good enough to book us a trip to Muir Woods and Sausalito which we really enjoyed. We opted to return to San Francisco by taking the ferry from Sausalito - giving us a spectacular view of the Golden Gate Bridge and Alcatraz.Considering we had never visited San Fransisco before we're really pleased with how well we did on choice of location and place to stay. We'd certainly stay at the Castle Inn again!

<Author>JB30
<Content>Good value in San Francisco Stayed for 3 nights at start of holiday. Service on desk was excellent. Room above average, clean and comfortable. Breakfast nothing fancy but decent start to the day.Located slightly away from everything but less than 20 mins walking distance to all main sights, bus stop just outside if you want to rest your legs after walking up and down the hills! <Author>PKWOnt_Canada
<Content>Perfect Location We stayed the last week of August in the Suite. It was a perfect room for us because of our two teenage boys. Very large suite, comfy k.size beds in both rooms. The kids had their own tv with two couches and we had a seperate bedroom with tv. and dresser drawers. There is a large walk in closet, with shelves for luggage and clothes, and a microwave and two!! mini-fridges. We did a deluxe city tour the first day and we were very happy with our choice of Castle Inn after touring the city. The Union Square area was recommended to us by a travel agent, however it is typical Big City downtown. Lots of nice stores for a day visit, but lots of bums and we wouldn't have felt safe there after dark. Castle Inn is located in what we considered a yuppy residential area and is close and within walking distance to Fish. Wharf, Pier 39, Alcatraz Ferry, Lombard etc. where we spent most of our time. Around the corner there is a drugstore, great restaurants, Starbucks, Tea Emporium and a Bank America with an ATM machine we felt safer using than the no-name ones at tourist spots. At the front desk Marshall and Arlene were VERY helpful with directions, bus routes, areas to avoid and areas to definitely see. Rooms are a little older but very clean. Suite is a little noisy because of traffic but when we were there at night we simply closed the windows and that helped alot. If you have an AAA or CAA membership you should get a better rate. We felt very safe at night in the area and the cab ride from the Wharf area is only about $6-$7, which we really only took advantage of a couple of times because we were tired. The cont. breakfast fed my 17 and 13 yr. old boys very nicely. It was more than enough food and they loved the hot choc. throughout the day. We used the local transit the most what with the bus route/transfers to all the tourist spots easy to catch around the corner from the hotel. The bus passes are a good deal, and they can also be used on the cable cars instead of paying per ride!!! (adds up quickly). We would definitely stay here again and will recommend Castle Inn to friends. I'm glad we trusted what was written on this site. Mississauga, Canada.

<Author>rsnow95
<Content>An Experience that is Difficult to Explain My wife and I visited SF for the first time and stayed at the Castle Inn (CI) for three nights. My initial impression at check in was that maybe we had selected accomodations that ran contrary to our tastes and preferences. We do not have any children and stay mostly at four-star hotels/resorts when we travel. In contrast, the CI is an older motel that has outward facing rooms. In the spirit of vacation, and based on user reviews, I kept an open mind. The rooms are what I would term economy, somewhat in the order of a Comfort Inn or a Motel 6. We found the room to be adequately clean. For those light sleepers, please keep in mind that the hotel is in the city. You will here normal traffic sounds and the rooms are not equipped with air conditioners. This is not uncommon in hotels/motels along the coast as the ocean breeze is used to cool the room. We were not bothered by the traffic and slept with the windows open the whole stay. While the rate may seem high relative to the accomodations, parking is free, which is a plus in a major metropolitan area. There is a coffee maker, microwave oven and refrigerator in the room. We particularly enjoyed having the refrigerator as it saved us alot of money on beverages.Two things that made our stay enjoyable here were: (1) the central location; and (2) Marshall, who provided us with alot of information on where and where not to go. We gathered advise from him almost daily, and based on his suggestions, we were even able to take the walking tour of Alcatraz, despite the fact it was listed as fully booked during the length of our stay.The location of CI is unique in that it is easy to get to all the major sights and attractions. Additionally, there are a range of places to eat within close proximity to the hotel (ranging from pizza to upscale casual dining), as well as a Walgreens within two blocks. Just ask Marshall for a suggestion. We found that the only time we were in our our room was to sleep, so we would not have used many of the ammenities found in higher-end hotels for this trip. There is just too much to see and do. Overall, we were happy with our stay at CI.  
<Date>Aug 29, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Save your money for a real san francisco experience My husband and I travel to San Francisco frequently. We usually stay in small hotels unique to the city. This time, along with a family member, we were traveling for a medical treatment. I chose this hotel based on reviews and location and reserved two rooms for two nights. When my surgery was cancelled and I called the hotel to see if we could make an adjustment as only my husband and myself needed one room for one night, all they could say was well, you have to pay for both rooms for both nights. No offer to try to rent the rooms. When we arrived and suggested that at least we could donate the rooms to a city agency for the needy, they were horrified and insisted that we should let them rent the rooms. One was rented for one night for half price. This hotel has a 72 hour cancellation policy which is self-serving and punitive. They appear to only care about tourists who are making one trip to San Francisco and to have no interest in cultivating follow-up business. Further, it turns out that this establishment is not a hotel but an aging standard motel. I recommend that tourists skip this place and pick one of the city's charming small hotels for a real San Francisco experience.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Comfortable  From check-in to departure three days later, The Castle Inn was perfect for us and Versa was incredibly helpful. Rooms are simple and clean. Nice to have a mini-fridge and microwave in the room for snacks and leftovers. Versa is a wonderful ambassador for San Francisco! Her restaurant recommendations were excellent (Polkers for breakfast and Habana, Hyde Street Seafood, and Ristorante Milano for dinner) and guidance on using cable cars and buses was extremely useful. Location is in a safe neighborhood that is centrally located for walking excursions to Chinatown, Coit Tower, Fisherman's Wharf, and Lombard St. If you want a great workout that will showcase some beautiful homes and views, take Broadway until you reach the Pacific Heights neighborhood. If you're looking for luxury this is not the place. But, if you are looking for a clean, comfortable, and friendly base for exploring SF, this is definitely the place!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Taste of San Francisco living. This is a great economical base for touring SF. We booked two rooms for three nights based on the glowing recommendations on this web site and were not disappointed. Hotel location is perfect. Easy walking distance to Ghiardelli Sq, but a little tougher (hills) to Fishermans Wharf, Pier 39, Chinatown, North Beach and Lombard St. Climb the hill and take the cable car to Union Sq.What I really liked was the neighborhood atmosphere. It gave a taste of what draws people to live in SF - a variety of great neighborhood restaurants around the corner on Polk St or Union St (try the Little Thai two doors down). Stroll around the corner in the morning and browse the bageleries, boulangeries, coffee shops and tea houses for breakfast - up and comming without being too chi-chi. Felt safe even late at night.I checked out some of the other hotels we were considering and was glad we stayed at the the Castle - the Cow Hollow motels are too far away and the Union Sq area is too busy and grimy - and twice the price. The Castle is quiet enough to sleep with the windows open and free come-and-go parking makes this the best deal in SF.Only problem - one of our rooms had a slight odour which we couldn't place. Room certainly looked clean and new and since we didn't report it we can't really blame the management.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very Satisfied!!! My sister and children and I stayed in The Castle Inn just before Memorial Day for a few nights and had a wonderful time. We were traveling on a budget and wanted to be safe and comfortable. While researching a place to stay in San Francisco, I noticed this Inn was the only place in this price range to receive consistant good reviews with no poor reviews. Sure, one lady complained about the color of the bathroom tiles, which I happened to like when I saw them. The tiles had a glazed rustic earthtone finish which only added to my experience because they weren't the same generic thing you see in every other Inn or Motel.It's true the Inn is run with 'Family Loving Care', we were given directions on how to get to places, places we should stay away from, etc. I would strongly advise if you are planning on walking to Fisherman's Wharf, which we did for the sake of exercise to retrace 'on the way back' the route you took there as laid out by Marshall. If you try to take a shortcut back to the Inn as we did from the north part of the Wharf by following the city map you will run into some mammoth hills that are so steep that the sidewalks are actually stairsteps. Let me just say that after that experience, all of the other walking exercises on our trip down along the coastline didn't seem nearly as challenging. After a 2 mile walk in Santa Barbara, we found ourselves saying to each other if we only had a good hill, like in San Fransisco...this is too easy! Also, be sure to wear comfortable and supportive athletic shoes. We never could have made it in street shoes or without the beautiful cool weather which greatly helped with the intensity of the workout required to return to the Inn from that direction.The front of the Inn has been painted a creamy yellow and is no longer grey as in the featured picture. The side of the Inn is layed out sort of like a multi-level La Quinta Inn, and I was a little worried because we had a lot of heavy luggage I knew we wouldn't be able to lug up the stairs. We were happy to discover they had an elevator along with handy rolling luggage carts. We had a room toward the back on the 2nd floor so the street noise was minimal. The parking garage was a squeeze but FREE, and we were prepared for that from reading previous reviews. Getting in is a challenge because it is a single car entry and once you get in, there are a few good places for a larger vehicle such as a van or SUV. The real trick is getting out which takes multiple manuverings, about 3 to 4 minutes worth and patience in getting the car into the correct position to head out, but since we walked or rode the trolley most of the time, we did not have to go in or out often. They also have an excellent camera system in the garage and covered stairway and elevator areas that is transmitted to the office which added to our feeling of safety. Never did we feel unsafe in this neighborhood and we walked to restaurants at night with two minor girls. They also had vending machines on the stair landings where you could get pop and bottled water for $1, you will pay $2.50 to $3.00 on the Wharf. If I had to change one thing, I would suggest that they extend their continental breakfast buffet time to 9:30 or 10:00am instead of 9:00am. which seemed a little early to me. We either had to procure our breakfast pastries early and store them in our room for after our walk or try to return from our early morning walks in time to partake of it before it shut down. We had a wonderful time visiting San Fransisco and staying at The Castle Inn was the best choice we could have made in this price range. We were not disappointed!! Keep up the good work Castle Inn and Good Luck!!!  
<Date>Jun 8, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>I will always stay here while in San Fran This hotel was amazing. Before I even got there I wanted to write a grand review. Varsa handled my reservation and was also on duty for the 3 nights me and my boyfriend stayed there, and she was extremely helpful from the first time I called to the time of checkout. We did not experience any problems while there. In fact, on the first day we returned to our room and the cleaning staff had left our window open to air the room out (screen was closed, though), so we went to the front desk to request that they not do this (just our own preference), and it was immediately put on the cleaning staff list of special instructions. Needless to say, the window was never left open again. The accommodations were perfect. If you're expecting rose petals in your bathroom and a foot massage with bon bons upon awakening, you a) may be spending too much time in your room anyway, but b) should look elsewhere, because these accommodations are great for people who want a good, safe, convenient location with good service (the fridge and microwave were a definite plus). If you're looking for the latter, then book here. The free parking was EXCELLENT. Buyer beware - if you think you're getting a bargain at some of the other hotels which do not have free parking, think again. You could pay upwards of $25+ per day for parking alone, and even more if they don't grant you in-and-out access during the day. Do the math and in most cases you'll probably come out dollars ahead if you stay here instead. There were some great restaurants in the area (Aroma Cafe and the Bagelry are worth special mention...and you MUST go to Firefly which is all the way across town but well worth it), as well as a Walgreens literally just around the corner (at the time of this review) in case you forgot something. For those who might be a little swayed by the one unsatisfied reviewer who complained that this hotel isn't as close to the Wharf as advertised, I'd say this -- downtown San Fran is not like Manhattan...it's pretty small and everything is fairly easy to get to. It took us about 20 min by cable car, including the walk from the hotel to the stop and the trip down to the wharf. Plus you get some great photo ops (including Lombard's one crooked block) that way! And in terms of being told to hold it down, the sign for quiet hours is clearly posted...I'd want a hotel manager to do the same thing if there were guests disturbing my sleep even if they didn't mean to. Again, this hotel was fabulous. Thanks to Varsha and Sy for a wonderful experience. I'll be back whenever I come to San Fran next, and will gladly recommend you to everyone I know!  
<Date>May 28, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent value We stayed at the Castle Inn for 6 nights in May and found that it was worthy of the good reviews we had seen on this site. Marshall, Arlene and Varsa were very friendly and helpful with suggestions and advice. The street map they gave us was very handy and helped us find our way around the city. The room was spotlessly clean and the beds were exceptionally comfortable. Our shower was really powerful and there was everything we needed in the room, fridge/freezer, iron and ironing board and microwave oven. Our room was one of the farthest away from the road and we weren't disturbed by traffic noise at all. The area was very convenient and we were able to walk to Fisherman's Wharf, (downhill all the way there, but not too bad on the way back) and Chinatown (steep hill but worth it for the view, or you can go through the tunnel instead).The breakfast was adequate for us and there are plenty of restaurants and shops nearby if you need more.If you don't need luxury you will find everything you need here with the bonus of having staff who make you welcome and will take time to answer your questions, advise and help you. It's also fantastic value, especially if you have a car as the parking is free.

<Author>IrishIWish
<Content>Look No Further..Stay At The Castle Inn! We just returned from 4 nights at The Castle Inn. For the budget minded traveler I can't recommend this place enough. It was everything we had hoped it would be.First and foremost the place was immaculate. I have stayed in far nicer hotels that weren't nearly as clean. Whether you were looking at the elevator, lobby area, common hallways, your room or bedding, everythingw as clean. Next, the hotel management was wonderful. Varsa was without a doubt the most accomodating person I've ever run across. She told us where to go, where not to go, and how to get there. She made dinner reservations for us, called cabs, booked tours, you name it. She was very personable and never made us feel badly for asking the same question more than once. (And trust me, we did!). She was always looking for feedback too, in terms of how we liked things, how we got around and so forth. She is obviously very dedicated to the success of The Castle Inn and it shows.Some folks have complained about the breakfasts. We found no problems whatsoever. Each day there was a choice of prepackaged breakfast bars, packaged muffins or pastries, yogurt, fresh fruit and coffee/tea/hot cocoa. It was more than enough to jump start our morning and energized us to begin our walks. If you are looking for a sit down breakast you won't find it here but like I said, you certainly will find enough choices to hold you over until you find a restaurant. I liked the fact that we could grab a banana or two and hit the road.The room itself was more than fine. We had 2 queens and also a roll-away. I think we may have been put in a larger room to accomodate the roll-away. Varsa warned us that the roll away might not be comortable but honestly, at the end of each day I was so dog tired I could hav slept on a bed of nails. The room had a/c and windows that slide open to let in the fresh air. We were not bothered by the city noises at all. Did we hear them? Yes. But it's noises we'd expect to hear in the city and we got use to them quickly.The room also had a nice micro and fridge. There are plenty of restaurants around the corner so if you choose to do take-out you can safely store your food in your room. There is also a Walgreens just around the corner for water, soda or other munchies you might want to stock in your room. The tub/shower/toilet were separate from the bathroom sink which allowed us to save time and do things in tandem. There was also a hairdryer and full sized ironing board and iron in the room, which unfortunatley we did have to use even though I vowed I wouldn't iron on vacation. I loved the location of the hotel too. It took us about 15 minutes (pretty much all downhill) to get to Ghiradelli Square. North Beach was also not a bad walk. There were bus routes about 2 blocks away (also an easy walk). We loved all the neighborhood restaurants and cafes too. After staying here, I'd never want to stay in Fisherman's Wharf or Union Square.We had a very positive experience at The Castle and would highly recommend it.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good Value, Great Neighbourhood As in San Fran week of April 3 to April 10th and we stayed at the Castle Inn. It truly was great value. The Inn staff was extremely helpful with where breakfast/dinner options in the neighbourhood, tour companies to use and places to go see ie. Wineries in Napa Valley. The rooms were basic but big compared to other hotels and you spend minimal time it doesn't really matter. Parking is included and that in itself is a hug help because even though everyone says you don't need a car in SF, we liked having it available to us to just drive to a neighbourhood and cruise around the less touristy places. The breakfast offered by the hotel (or any of the hotels, we also stayed at the Buena Vista Motor Inn as well) isn't much to talk about. Muffins and Danishes that are packaged (trans fats), cereal bars, bananas and apples (good) orange juice and coffee but it came in handy a couple of days.The location of this hotel is ideal. Very prominent homes nearby but it did feel like the streets were very steep in Russian Hill. Bus routes are extremely convenient. Hop on to the VanNess #47 to get to Fisherman's warf and downtown. Polk St right by the hotel has a Bagel shop for a breakfast on the run and Polker for a sitdown breakfast - you must try the Skillet with sausage. Stay away from Market St. and the Tenderloin area...seedy part of town. There's lots to do in SF so have fun.Cathy, Hamilton, Ontario

<Author>kbrwriter
<Content>Great - except for the street noise Based on Trip Advisor reviews, I booked a five-day stay here in early February. The hotel lived up to its billing -- except for the street noise. My room was as far back from the street as it got, and I still heard motorcycles and cars gunning down Broadway at all hours of the night. Other than that, I have only praise for the hotel. You can't beat the price; after tax, I paid $90/night through Orbitz. The hotel was not just clean but fastidiously so; an employee was out sweeping the sidewalk in the early morning. The room was quite large, especially since I was traveling solo. I felt very safe; the garage was especially well secured with alarms and cameras. The staff handled my every request before and during my arrival without hesitation: late checkout, receipt of faxes and packages, etc. The free parking was wonderful. And the location was fantastic. Broadway and Van Ness are convenient thoroughfares for getting around town, and there are lots of great restaurants and bars within walking distance. (Check out the great wine bar at the back of William Cross Wine Merchants - 2253 Polk Street. Say Hi to Jeremy, the owner, for me!) Overall, a good budget hotel for exploring the city!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Keep In Mind As others, I did see the positive reviews for the Castle Inn. I thought I'd give it a try, booking it through Orbitz, based on the Orbitz three-star rating it had at the time. I would just like people to have realistic expectations of this property. This is a two-star motel, not a three-star hotel (like the Holiday Inn at Fisherman's Wharf). It has exterior corridors. The room was spacious and clean, but the room I was assigned smelt of cleaner, and it definitely had a motel-type feel to it. Free parking is a big deal in San Francisco. However, the motel's parking is cramped, and I wouldn't advise parking a SUV there (at least not for the faint of heart). The staff was extremely nice, so I feel bad not writing a glowing review as so many others did here.  If you're looking for value in a property situated in town, and you don't mind a motel, than consider the Castle Inn. Otherwise, I would look elsewhere. If you look hard enough, you can get a main chain three-star hotel for just a bit more per night. The Castle Inn wasn't anything exceptional. My main problem with the property was that it was billed as something more than it was -- a motel.   
<Date>Feb 10, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Mom and Pop Gem for City Folks Stayed two nights in January, '05 during perfect sunny weather. This older property has been meticulously renovated with quality materials and attention to detail (e.g., crown moldings in main room and patterned tile work in bath), even though choice of colors and materials of drapery/decor could have been better handled. Not tacky, just off in taste and execution a bit. But you forget about that when you experience how well-managed the hotel is and how great a location the Castle occupies for forays into San Francisco and surrounding environs. The hotel structure's layout is a brilliant urban solution, as the building is slotted into its space on Broadway with three tiers of rooms all facing West, with two levels of parking off the street. The front desk is up one level from Broadway and controls (more or less) ingress and egress to the elevator, stairs, and upper garage (I'd say, as a New Yorker/LAXer, that it's a good security arrangement). Rearward rooms are quieter with stairs there. The third floor view picks up a lovely old grey stone church directly and in the distance the upper sections of the Golden Gate Br. can be seen. The district the Castle is situated in abounds in great prepared food (try Pesce for nouveau Italian tapas and Polkers for great breakfasts and burgers), wine and liquor shops, fresh fruit, coffee, conveniences, and general down-to-earth S.F.-style residential living; the Castle is within walking distance to other areas of interest, and of course the buses and cable cars are right there too. I didn't bother with the rental car in S.F. Managers Arlene and Marshall are charming, knowledgeable, humane, no-nonsense hotel professionals and San Franciscoans who welcome mature, city-savvy, responsible guests looking to explore and enjoy one of the world's great metropoles and regions. If that's you and co., you'll appreciate this uber-urban, basic, but in what it offers, high-quality and smart guest house.  
<Date>Jan 27, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic hotel I stayed here for 4 nights in mid December 04 and I loved the place. The free parking was fantastic, always a space and easy to get in and out of. The room was one a good size, the bathroom was a little old, but better than a lot of hotels I've been in (and they cost more). The room was quiet, we heard a little noise from people walking by the door as it's an outside corridor, but not enough for it to bother us. The windows also opened up which is rare for a hotel, but great for fresh air. The staff were SO helpfull. They gave us a map and wrote down the places to avoid at night, the places to eat cheaply, where the laundry was, where Kinko's was, anything you needed to know they knew. The hotle is within walking distance of almost everything you want to see adn do, Fishermans Wharf, Pier 39, street cars, cafe's, bars, Wallgreens.Overall this was one of the best hotels I stayed in the US (we stayed in 9) and one of the cheapest. I would stay here again next time I'm in San Francisco and have told all my friends to stay here as well. Great hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>More than pleasantly surprised This November my wife and I decided to drive up the coast to San Francisco. We did not make reservations and decided to take our chances. Walking around the Fisherman's Wharf we decided to check out the accommodations recommended at the California Welcome Center. We were directed to a wall with listings of accommodations and a phone to call them. We tried a couple of places but no luck or they did not sound good. The fellow in attendance said for us to try the Castle Inn as he had heard good things from others about it. The person answering the phone I believe was Marshall. He began to tell me how wonderful the Castle Inn was. He kept telling me and telling me and telling me all the wonderful things about the Castle Inn. I did not get their names but on the business card it says Marshall and Ariene. I assume they were the ones I dealt with. They were very helpful and more than accommodating.  If we are in San Francisco again we most certainly stay there and we will wholeheartedly recommend Castle Inn to others. The location was quite close to the trolley cars and easily accessable.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Pros and cons Decided to discover San Francisco during it's low peak season which is during the holidays. SF is beautifully decorated during this time too. We stayed 3 nights on early Dec. Got a great deal from --------------. Pros :- Price : it was about $60 for a king-sized bed with amenities like a fridge, m/w and FREE parking.- Location : it had some interesting places to see around it like the Haas-Lilenthal house and Spreckel's Mansion (Danielle Steele's house). It's also a few blocks away from Union Street which is all lighted up for the holidays. Octagon House is on this street corner too. Walk around Polk St to find interesting shops and breakfast places. For the discerning Muslim eaters, there is a Halal Deli nearby too. Last but not least, Walgreens is half a block away.- Common sense deposit : the deposit was $25. I thought I was hearing things.- Public transportation : easy walk to bus and cable car lines.- Room : Clean room. Had a nice fragrant smell when we checked in. TV with a VCR. Had a nice little breakfast table in there. It's really a spacious room and I think recent furniture. This was on the first level so below us was the parking lot and the rooms face some buildings. The good part about that is that we don't face the main road so practically no noise at night. The only noises came from the common coridor when people pass by, and we have an adjoining room so we hear them even though it's locked. Hardly hear the people from upstairs though. Lots of light.- Bathroom : Good water pressure and very clean. Good light.- Good communication : I e-mailed them to ask to inquire about my room and the response was quick and informative. I had requested a top floor room and a king size bed but only got the king size bed as the rooms I book was specially reserved for the travel company I used. However, they gave me options for an upgrade if I needed more privacy. I chose to stay with the room I got just to see what it's like (which I'm quite pleased with).- Vending machines : The drinks were $1 each. Cons :- Bathroom : It's really small and had brownish tiles which I'm not too keen of. It's a bit tight for me but good enough for a shower. If they are thinking of a renovation, I would suggest to increase the size a bit and change the tile colors to white. - Sink and closet area : This area looks like it belongs in the 70's (including bathroom). The closet rods are a bit rusted and the sink tiles are the same brown as the bathroom. Not much space to hang clothes but they had the luggage holder so I just used my bag to hold my clothes.- Towels : A bit rough and I guess it's a standard size for a bath towel but seemed a bit small for me.- Check-out time : I thought the check out time was 12pm but it's actually at 11am. Still, they gave a warning call which was really nice but still which I had the extra hour though. They didn't charge me the extra minutes I needed to pack.All in all, my husband and I are pretty happy with Castle Inn. It's not featured in most of the travel books we saw so it's good that we read about it here in tripadvisor. Have fun in SF!  
<Date>Dec 23, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Location This was the first time for us in San Francisco, and we didn't know where to stay. After reading many reviews on this web site, I came across the Castle Inn. I had a good feeling about this hotel. I had already made reservations with another hotel and cancelled them. <Author>MyBoysRule
<Content>The most wonderful owners We stayed at the Castle in on December 10th based on the reviews on this site. The hotel is very easy to find with easy and free parking (amazing in SF). The room was basic but very, very clean, spacious, quiet and had a large bathroom and even a mini fridge and microwave.What makes this place special, however, are the owners. We were considering a late night check-in so I called to ask how late we could arrive. Although their front desk closes at 11:00 PM, they were happy to accomodate us with a midnight check-in and, in fact, felt bad that we did not take them up on their offer to wait up for us. When we arrived we were greeted with the biggest smile and a very warm reception by Varsa - it felt like we were old friends coming for a visit. We were checked in quickly, given a map of the city with instructions on which areas to stay away from and directions on how to get to our restaurant. They only had a room for one night so Varsa made a call to get us into another hotel for the next night.In the morning, I came down to get some coffee and muffins and was asked how our evening had been, how we slept and then Varsa gave me a tray to carry breakfast up to our room. It is these very small and thoughtful details that make the Castle Inn special.We will most certainly be back on our next stay.

<Author>akvavitOhio
<Content>Great Neighborhood, Better Proprietor! I was attending a conference at the nearby Holiday Inn on California and Van Ness. Since the rate there was $40 a night more than the Castle Inn, I decided to spend three nights after the conference at the Castle Inn, based upon the recommendations posted here.Smart move! First, the co-owner, Varsa, is one of the nicest, helpful hotel operators I've ever met. She's definitely on par with the best BB proprietors I've encountered abroad. The hotel is budget-minded, so don't expect a breakfast spread or other luxuries. However, Varsa will give you a great orientation to the neighborhood and the public transportation system, which was much more helpful than what I got from the Holiday Inn. I only had a few days, but managed to navigate the public transportation system thanks to her help and cheat sheet on where to pick up the appropriate buses, etc.The room was spacious, clean and, for a room with a view of the road (Broadway), reasonably quiet. The TV had more cable channels than at the Holiday Inn, if that's important to you. It also had a fridge and microwave, which was a plus! However, no utensils, so bring your own bottle opener or corkscrew.Which brings me to another big plus -- the neighborhood! This section of Nobb Hill is everything you'd want while on vacation. It's close to the bus, tram, and trolley lines. There's a Walgreens around the corner if you forget something, and a 24-hour Kinkos on Van Ness if you need to check your e-mail. There's a wine bar, a pub, and a great Thai restaurant, all within a block or so. There are plenty of coffee shops, and even a great crepe restaurant. Varsa is expecting baby #3, but if she's there, be sure to ask her for recommendations on where to eat, where to shop, etc.Also, if you need a transfer to the airport, Varsa will arrange it for you, even if you need to be picked up before the office opens at 7 a.m. (the bus costs $12 one way).You just can't beat the price, value, convenience, and location! I'll definitely return next time I visit the Bay area.  
<Date>Dec 13, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very Pleased. We stayed at the Castle Inn from October 18 - 22 2004. We booked a room here based on reviews we read on TripAdvisor. Coming from a small city to a large area like San Francisco, we were stepping outside our comfort zone so one of our main concerns was finding a safe place to stay in a safe neighborhood. A second concern was finding a reasonably priced hotel which would allow us to spend our extra cash on tours, attractions, restaurants - in short, on experiencing the city. The Castle Inn exceeded our expectations in both areas. We felt safe, and we were able to stay four days in a clean, comfortable, reasonably priced hotel. We walked EVERYWHERE from this hotel - Fisherman's Wharf, Chinatown, the Trans America Building, Coit Tower, Lombard Street, the Palace of Fine Arts, Fort Point, and the Golden Gate. Granted, some of these were rather long hikes, but we were still so pleased not to have to worry about transportation and really experience the city on foot.We enjoyed meeting and talking to Arlene, Marshall, and Varsa. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We made a great choice in the Castle Hotel Early in August I took my nephew to San Francisco. After reviewing many hotels on the internet, I chose the Castle based on the number of favorable reviews. We were not dissappointed. It is not the Hilton, but then we are not Hilton people. Our hosts, Matthew and Arlene, were absolutely the best tour guides you could hope for. They knew when it was easier to take the bus, a car, or just walk. Matthew was instrumental in getting us tickets for Alcatraz, as we were silly enough not to purchase in advance. The location could not be beat. We walked almost everywhere and late at night, too. Never did we feel unsafe. When it was easier to take a bus, one on the main bus lines was just around the corner. We drove down and parking was included in the more than reasonable price (for San Francisco). A small breakfast was included with the room. Which, by the way, was clean and included a small fridge, coffee maker, and hair dryer. As you can see, I have no problem recommending the Castle. I'm only sorry I did not have time to write my review previously.

<Author>TaskForceRanger
<Content>met my expectation I chose to stay at this hotel because of all the excellent reviews I read at tripadvisor. I am not sure whether all the excellent reviews are *real*, however what I can say is that - this inn is average and - the inn has met my expectation. * STAFF - excellent - friendly staff* LOCATION - average - Definitely NOT walking distance to the wharf or Chinatown. You won't want to walk it, even the 2.5 blocks to the cable car are long and steep. I drove around the city, so it was not a probably for me.* SAFETY - average - the area seems relatively safe. However, I am a bit uncomfortable with the fact that anyone can take the elevator or stairs up/down without passing through the office or front entrance. And the main office closes at 11pm. * AMENTITIES - average - towels are clean, but feel a bit used. The frig, microwave are pluses!!!* HOUSEKEEPING - excellent - room is very clean.* PRICE - excellent ($85 weekday, $95 weekend)* PARKING - excellent - it's free. It's a bit tight getting in and out, but hey, it's free!* BREAKFAST - OK - nothing to rave about, they serve packaged pastries and granola bars! The only good thing I got was a banana.

<Author>TripKid
<Content>Great SF Home Base!!! We stayed here for two nights during the week and were very satisfied with the room. The rooms are clean and basic, and included a fridge and microwave. Also, included each morning was a small continental breakfast available at the office. And, to my surprise, the friendly staff gave us some tourist advice! The big benefit to the Castle Inn was the free parking. Parking - a rare commodity in San Francisco. The secret to seeing San Francisco is using the public transportation. We left our car at the Castle Inn the whole time during our stay. The only issue with the Castle Inn is that it's not that close to the major attractions like Chinatown and Fisherman's Wharf. It's walkable, but it would be a very long walk. But, you can get anywhere in the City by public bus - only takes a few minutes. We'll look forward to staying at the Castle Inn in the future! Bon Voyage!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great location, friendly staff The Castle Inn is in a safe area that is not yet overrun by oodles of tacky tourist traps. We felt safe to walk around there in the evening with our daughter. There are great restaurants and cafes nearby where you can blend in with the locals. The variety of food on nearby Polk St. is astonishing from morning to evening. You are sure to find something to please everyone.The Inn is located a couple of blocks away from one of the cable car lines, and Fisherman's Wharf is a relatively short walk away. It's central, but not in a district where tourists are prey for panhandlers or pickpockets.It's a clean, inexpensive place to stay where the staff is friendly and helpful. One huge asset also is their parking, as this is not always easy to come by in SF.I definitely recommend the Castle Inn for price, cleanliness, location and safety.

<Content>It was great. We stayed 3 nights here in July. It has to be the best kept secret in San Francisco. The city bus line is a few steps away, the cable car line was 3 blocks away and there are several restaurants and other amenities in the near-by area. <Author>Bid Ruth
<Content>Excellent Hideaway in the Middle of the City Look no further - this is the place to stay in San Francisco! We just returned from a four day stay for our tenth anniversary. The price is VERY reasonable, especially for the location and service.The rooms were clean and spacious with a separate room with a (useful) fridge and microwave. They are within walking distance of Ghirardelli Square, Chinatown, Fishermans Wharf and close to both Muni and Cable Car stops. Sy an Varsa were very helpful - assisting us in picking the perfect place for a romantic dinner. The breakfast could have been a little more healthful, but nice that they have something available. If you are looking for a hearty breakfast try Bay Watch Restaurant (2150 Lombard Street - west of Van Ness near Filmore). If you have a car the free parking is a deal. For travel within San Francisco, you're much better off to leave your car parked and head out on foot or transit. We took BART and a Cable Car to and from the airport. If you want to use your credit card to purchase BART tickets you have to purchase them in $10.00 increments. Something I'm sure they do to screw tourists out of 10 cents each with a fare of $4.95 each way. Also, don't bother waiting in line at Powell Street Station (or any other starting point) for the Cable Car. Walk up a block or two and you will catch one much quicker. You can purchase a three day muni pass for $15.00 which is good on both muni buses and cable cars. Another word to the wise. If you ever find yourself needing to walk up an intense hill, walk a block or two in either direction and it's sure to be easier.Great City, Great Hotel, Great Service! While you're visiting the west coast, why not visit Vancouver too? You won't be disappointed.Brad  Karen

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Absoluteley superb We spent 8 days at the Castle Inn during June as part of our 6 weeks honeymoon of Hawaii and the west coast.This motel/hotel has very little to argue against it. In fact we could think of nothing! Location is superb, bus stop just out on Van Ness, and the Powell Hyde cable car route two blocks along Broadway. We were staying for a week, so we purchased a $20 transport pass from the fishermans wharf cable car turntable, and with the bus and cable car options close by, the hotel is extremely well located, and in a safe area. The Thai restaurant on the corner was great and cheap, get the takeaway and bring back to your room. The Star of India around the corner has a buffet for $8 which was the best Indian we've had in a while.Use the microwave to heat your left overs.Versa and the other staff are a wealth of information. If we ever come back to SFC, the Castle Inn will be our place to stay without question.David  Maria Burt, Wingan Way, Morwell Australia

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We'll return on our next trip to SF We stayed at the Castle Inn during our recent two day stay in SF, and it felt like our home away from home. First of all, we arrived on a late flight, getting into SFO at 11:15pm. I checked with them on the phone before hand to find out if we could check in that late. They said they normally closed at 11, but would be happy to wait for us, just that we call them when we arrive at the airport. It was around 1 am when we finally arrived at the hotel, and we were happily greeted with friendly and helpful service. One of my sons brought his laptop computer along and the next day, the proprieters helped him on his computer to get the wireless networking working correctly. She even called our room later to see how we made out and how things were working (they worked well.) We were also able to leave our car parked at the hotel while we toured SF mostly on foot. On our final day, even though checkout time was around noon, we were on the boat trip to Alcatraz until the mid afternoon, and our hosts said it would be no problem to leave our car parked at the hotel through the afternoon, until we were done so we wouldn't have to pay for parking around the wharf. If we return to SF, we'll return to the Castle Inn - nice people!

<Content>The Castle Inn was great! When making accommodation plans for a trip to San Francisco, we were looking for a moderately priced hotel in a good location. <Author>Kander007
<Content>Excellent value Spent three days at the Castle Inn, May 24 -27 and found it to be a good value. Rooms were well appointed with all the essentials for a tourist on the go including an iron and ironing board. Really clean...in fact, I don't think my bathroom is as clean as I found there. Tub and shower a might small but as with everything else, we were more interested in seeing the city then the walls of the room. Some noise from the street, but it didn't keep me from getting a good night's sleep. Staff was very friendly and helpful with directions and recommendations. Located within walking distance to restaurants, taverns, and a Walgreens on Polk Ave. Also about two blocks from a cable car stop and other mass transit near by.Overall, a fairly good stay. FYI: Mass transit is probably the best way to go for the majority of sightseeing, but you are best advised to be prepared for crushing conditions on some lines especially into Chinatown. Also, best to stay off during the school rush hour between 3 and 5 p.m. as we found some of the most unruly and arrogent children in the country aboard. (If this is the flower of American youth, we should be really scared about the future.)

<Author>Seanhoya
<Content>Not fit for a king, but certainly fit for a tourist! Our stay at the Castle Inn was truly pleasant - an experience that we hope soon to repeat. The location was perfect - it was within walking distance of all major sites, if you don't mind the occasional San Francisco hill. My wife and I spent four days using The Castle Inn as our base from which we walked San Francisco. Our room was simple and clean - the refrigerator was nice to keep our bottled water cold. The management was very helpful, more than once offering advice on how to get to our daily destinations. Parking was a breeze with the two lower lots. Our opinion of the Castle Inn was that it was clean, safe, convenient, and above all, priced well. For the price, I don't think that there is a better deal in San Francisco! That being said, there were a few things that bothered us - we couldn't get the elevator to work until the third day we were there (being on the second floor, it wasn't much of an inconvenience), the parking garage had this horrible ear-piercing alarm that went off everytime we walked into it, and finally, our room fan created this horrible noise whenever we had it on. Overall, however, we enjoyed our stay, and will certainly think of The Castle Inn first when we go back to San Francisco.

<Author>NE_Wayfarer
<Content>I'll be back I was in California on business, so I added a few personal days to visit my favorite city. The Castle Inn was in a great location, away from the chaos of Union Square and the Disneyland of Fisherman's Wharf, but close enough to catch a cable car or walk about a bit. What particularly sold me on the Castle Inn was the included on-site parking. Anywhere else, you'd end up spending $25/day (or more), and have to deal with the hastle of getting your car in and out, but the ability to hop in my car and take off to distant destinations was a great plus.The rooms were modest, comfortable and clean. The area was safe and quiet. Varsa, the concierge, was terrific. She has a great knowledge of the city, was very helpful, and was just generally charming. I believe there was a continental breakfast included, but I opted to go down the block to Polk St. for great coffee at Peet's. Forget about Starbuck's!This motel is not fancy, but it's a great deal. I hope to come back with my family soon. There's a huge suite that can accomodate a large family.(Just a hint-I think if you call the Inn directly you can get a better rate than the online deals-Ask for Varsa!)

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>An exceptional facility, value and hosts Before traveling through Europe using Rick Steves' travel guides and philosophy where he promotes staying near the center of urban areas, we assiduously avoided these locations as overpriced, ill kept, and unsafe. We nearly let our past beliefs dictate where we would locate when we visited San Francisco. To our delight we found the Castle Inn to be a great value, fantastic location, fastidiously maintained and providing a secure parking area for our car--all inclusive in the price of the room. Our room looked recently redecorated and contained a refrigerator, coffee maker, microwave, a king size bed with an excellent mattress, and a table and chairs that offered an inviting place to read or update our travel log.Our hosts, Marshall  Arlene, were exceptional. They made us feel like valued friends. They provided us with maps, a suggested itinerary of things to see during our stay, and a detailed sheet of the various modes of public transportation listing the stops and fares. They made reservations for us for the tours we wanted to take and even found discount coupons for us in various travel guides. When we asked for advice on places to eat, they offered a compendium of choices depending on our ethnic choices--all within walking distances of the Castle Inn. The continental breakfasts they served were fresh, tasty, pleasantly presented and replenished right up to the end of the serving hours. Because of Marshall  Arlene's attentiveness and attention to detail and the needs of their guests, we assumed that they were the owners of the property rather than employees of the facility. I would suggest to the owners that they have a rare find in these two people. They should also be on the payroll of the Chamber of Commerce; they exude a love and enthusiasm for San Francisco that is infectious to anyone entering the motel to inquire of a vacancy.Thanks for making our stay so memorable. With your help we, too, left our hearts in San Francisco!  
<Date>Mar 13, 2004
